=== STEP 0 ===
<USER_REQUEST>
You are working in the repository:

dp-core-phase1-substrate-v3

TASK
Implement and execute the MLC v0.1 Pilot Experiment Protocol.

CONTEXT

The MLC v0.1 implementation phase is CLOSED.

The following are already implemented and must not be redesigned:

- progressive epistemic lifecycle
- Compilation Gate
- COMPILATION_REJECTED terminal state
- Evidence Ledger
- intrinsic measurement
- Evaluation Readiness
- frozen candidates
- prospective validation
- ADMIT / REJECT / DEFER decision logic
- DEFER taxonomy
- Belief Memory
- B1–B4 baselines
- ERC checkpoints
- validity Gates 1–10
- structured H1–H5 scientific result representation
- derived summary labels
- artifact persistence and run manifests

The purpose of this task is NOT to improve MLC.

The purpose is to implement and execute a pilot that determines whether the planned primary experiment is scientifically executable and adequately powered.

DO NOT redesign the architecture.
DO NOT tune MLC based on pilot outcomes.
DO NOT change scientific semantics silently.
DO NOT modify thresholds after observing pilot results.
DO NOT add mechanisms inspired by external architectures.
DO NOT attempt to make MLC succeed.

The pilot must preserve the possibility that the primary experiment will convincingly fail.

============================================================
1. PRIMARY RESEARCH QUESTION
============================================================

The eventual primary experiment asks:

Does prospective validation add measurable epistemic value over retrospective-only evaluation?

The pilot does NOT answer this question.

The pilot exists only to validate:

1. synthetic world generation,
2. class and zone composition,
3. estimator behavior,
4. paired-comparison variance,
5. minimum detectable effects,
6. power of the planned primary experiment,
7. artifact completeness,
8. scientific evaluator execution.

Pilot results must not be interpreted as evidence for or against MLC empirical value.

============================================================
2. PILOT SIZE
============================================================

Execute:

100 total synthetic worlds.

The pilot is exploratory for variance/power estimation only.

The planned primary experiment is currently:

500 total synthetic worlds.

However, n=500 is NOT yet frozen.

The pilot must estimate whether 500 worlds provide adequate power for the pre-registered minimum meaningful effects.

============================================================
3. WORLD ZONES
============================================================

Generate worlds from three explicit zones:

A. CLEAR ZONE

Purpose:
Test behavior comfortably away from decision boundaries.

Target allocation:

30% of worlds.

Include true ADMIT and true REJECT worlds.

Effects must be sufficiently separated from the frozen thresholds to represent clear decisions.

B. BOUNDARY ZONE

Purpose:
Stress-test behavior near the frozen decision thresholds.

Target allocation:

50% of worlds.

Frozen thresholds:

ADMIT_THRESHOLD = 0.15
REJECT_THRESHOLD = -0.05

Required true effect values:

-0.08
-0.04
 0.00
 0.05
 0.12
 0.16
 0.20

Ground-truth mapping must be:

-0.08 → REJECT

-0.04 → DEFER / EFFECT_AMBIGUITY
 0.00 → DEFER / EFFECT_AMBIGUITY
 0.05 → DEFER / EFFECT_AMBIGUITY
 0.12 → DEFER / EFFECT_AMBIGUITY

 0.16 → ADMIT
 0.20 → ADMIT

The pilot must use multiple independent seeds per effect value.

Do not use a single seed per boundary point.

Allocate boundary worlds as evenly as practically possible across the seven effect values.

Persist:

effect value,
seed,
ground-truth decision,
ground-truth DEFER subtype where applicable.

C. EVIDENCE-LIMITED ZONE

Purpose:
Test whether MLC correctly refuses commitment under insufficient evidence.

Target allocation:

20% of worlds.

Ground truth:

DEFER / EVIDENCE_LIMITED

The evidence-limited mechanism must remain scientifically distinct from effect ambiguity.

============================================================
4. REQUIRED ZONE COMPOSITION
============================================================

Target pilot composition:

Clear:             30 worlds
Boundary:          50 worlds
Evidence-limited:  20 worlds

Total:            100 worlds

Minor allocation differences inside the Boundary Zone are permitted only when required to distribute seeds across seven effect values.

The final exact allocation must be persisted before execution.

============================================================
5. WORLD GENERATION FREEZE
============================================================

Before executing MLC:

1. generate the complete pilot world registry,
2. assign all world IDs,
3. assign all seeds,
4. assign all zones,
5. assign true effects,
6. assign ground-truth decisions,
7. assign DEFER subtypes where applicable,
8. persist the complete registry,
9. hash the registry.

After the registry is frozen:

NO world may be added,
removed,
reclassified,
or regenerated based on observed MLC results.

============================================================
6. HYPOTHESES
============================================================

Preserve the existing H1–H5 structure.

H1:
Does the lifecycle execute with architectural fidelity?

H2:
Does MLC perform above the matched random baseline?

H3:
Does prospective validation improve decision accuracy relative to B2 retrospective-only evaluation?

H4:
Does prospective validation reduce catastrophic false admission relative to B2?

H5:
How well calibrated is DEFER behavior?

Do not redefine these hypotheses.

============================================================
7. H3 MANDATORY DISAGGREGATION
============================================================

Overall decision accuracy remains the pre-registered H3 endpoint.

Do not replace it.

However, because the pilot and primary experiment intentionally contain a high proportion of Boundary and Evidence-Limited worlds, pooled accuracy may be dominated by DEFER behavior.

Therefore the following zone-level accuracy breakdown is MANDATORY:

- Clear Zone accuracy
- Boundary Zone accuracy
- Evidence-Limited Zone accuracy

Compute these for:

- MLC
- B2 retrospective baseline
- B3 matched random baseline
- B4 Oracle where meaningful

For MLC vs B2, report paired accuracy differences for:

- pooled worlds,
- Clear Zone,
- Boundary Zone,
- Evidence-Limited Zone.

These are mandatory scientific disaggregations.

They do not replace H3.

Do not reinterpret a pooled H3 result without reporting where the observed difference originates.

============================================================
8. H4 CATASTROPHIC FALSE ADMISSION
============================================================

Preserve the pooled catastrophic false admission rate.

Definition:

MLC decides ADMIT when ground truth is:

- REJECT,
- DEFER / EVIDENCE_LIMITED,
- DEFER / EFFECT_AMBIGUITY.

Also report the mandatory decomposition:

1. false_admit_reject
2. false_admit_evidence_limited
3. false_admit_effect_ambiguous

Report each for:

- MLC
- B2

The pooled H4 result must never be reported without this decomposition.

============================================================
9. H5
============================================================

H5 remains orthogonal to H2–H4.

Report:

- DEFER precision
- DEFER recall
- EVIDENCE_LIMITED subtype accuracy
- EFFECT_AMBIGUITY subtype accuracy
- confusion matrix where applicable

Do not invent H5 success thresholds.

Existing provisional H5 targets, if present in code or documentation, must remain explicitly labeled provisional and must not be treated as scientifically justified thresholds.

============================================================
10. MINIMUM MEANINGFUL EFFECTS
============================================================

The pilot must estimate power for the planned primary experiment.

The scientific freeze must distinguish:

A. existing decision thresholds:

ADMIT_THRESHOLD = 0.15
REJECT_THRESHOLD = -0.05

These are design parameters.

B. minimum meaningful comparative effects for H2–H4.

Use the currently specified pilot protocol value of:

5 percentage points absolute paired difference

as the provisional minimum meaningful effect for:

- H2 accuracy advantage over B3,
- H3 accuracy advantage over B2,
- H4 catastrophic false admission reduction vs B2.

If the repository currently contains a different explicitly frozen value, STOP and report the conflict.

Do not silently choose between conflicting specifications.

============================================================
11. POWER TARGET
============================================================

Freeze the required statistical power target as:

80%.

The pilot must estimate whether the planned n=500 primary experiment provides at least 80% power to detect the provisional 5 percentage-point minimum meaningful paired effect.

Use pilot-observed paired outcome variance/correlation where appropriate.

Report power estimates separately for:

- H2
- H3
- H4

Also report the assumptions and method used for each power calculation.

If n=500 fails to achieve 80% estimated power for any hypothesis:

DO NOT tune the experiment silently.

Report:

- achieved estimated power,
- estimated sample size required for 80% power,
- uncertainty/limitations of the estimate.

The pilot may recommend a revised primary sample size.

It may not silently change it.

============================================================
12. NO_DIFFERENCE VS INCONCLUSIVE
============================================================

Preserve the distinction:

NO_DIFFERENCE:
The experiment has adequate power to detect the pre-registered minimum meaningful effect, but the observed comparison does not support improvement or degradation beyond the defined decision rule.

INCONCLUSIVE:
The experiment lacks adequate power or precision to distinguish the minimum meaningful effect.

The pilot itself must not generate final empirical H2–H4 verdict claims.

Its role is to estimate whether the planned primary design can later support NO_DIFFERENCE rather than merely INCONCLUSIVE.

============================================================
13. MULTIPLE COMPARISONS POLICY
============================================================

Freeze the following policy:

No family-wise multiplicity correction will be applied across H2, H3, and H4.

Reason:

H2, H3, and H4 are separate, fixed, pre-registered, non-adaptive scientific questions.

They are not selected after observing results.

Each hypothesis must therefore be interpreted independently using its pre-registered comparison and uncertainty interval.

This policy must be written explicitly into the pilot protocol artifact.

Do not add Bonferroni, FDR, or other multiplicity correction without stopping and reporting a specification conflict.

============================================================
14. STATISTICAL COMPARISONS
============================================================

Use paired comparisons wherever MLC and a baseline evaluate the same worlds.

At minimum compute:

H2:
MLC vs B3 matched random

H3:
MLC vs B2 retrospective-only

H4:
MLC catastrophic false admission vs B2

Report:

- point estimate,
- paired difference,
- uncertainty interval,
- pilot-observed variance,
- power estimate for n=500,
- estimated n required for 80% power.

Do not derive scientific success/failure claims from the pilot.

============================================================
15. PILOT VALIDITY GATES
============================================================

Implement pilot-specific validity gates.

At minimum:

PILOT_GATE_1_WORLD_COUNT

Exactly 100 worlds exist.

PILOT_GATE_2_ZONE_COMPOSITION

World allocation matches the frozen pilot registry.

PILOT_GATE_3_BOUNDARY_MAPPING

Every boundary effect maps to the correct frozen ground truth.

PILOT_GATE_4_MULTIPLE_SEEDS

Every boundary effect value has multiple independent seeds.

PILOT_GATE_5_REGISTRY_FREEZE

Executed worlds exactly match the hashed pre-run registry.

PILOT_GATE_6_THRESHOLD_FREEZE

ADMIT_THRESHOLD = 0.15
REJECT_THRESHOLD = -0.05
REJECT_THRESHOLD < ADMIT_THRESHOLD

PILOT_GATE_7_NO_SCIENTIFIC_MUTATION

No scientific thresholds, world labels, decision formulas, evidence formulas, or prospective-validation semantics changed during pilot implementation.

PILOT_GATE_8_ARTIFACT_COMPLETENESS

All required artifacts exist.

PILOT_GATE_9_PAIRED_COMPARISON_COMPLETENESS

Every eligible world has matched MLC/B2/B3 records.

PILOT_GATE_10_ZONE_METRIC_COMPLETENESS

Pooled and all mandatory zone-level metrics exist.

PILOT_GATE_11_CATASTROPHIC_DECOMPOSITION

The pooled H4 metric and all three mandatory sub-rates exist.

PILOT_GATE_12_POWER_REPORT_COMPLETENESS

H2, H3, and H4 each contain:

- pilot effect estimate,
- paired variance estimate,
- estimated n=500 power,
- estimated sample size for 80% power.

============================================================
16. REQUIRED ARTIFACTS
============================================================

Write artifacts to:

artifacts/experiments/mlc_v0_1_pilot/<run_id>/

Required artifacts:

1. pilot_protocol.json
2. pilot_world_registry.json
3. pilot_world_registry_hash.json
4. pilot_ground_truth.json
5. pilot_results.csv
6. pilot_mlc_decisions.json
7. pilot_baseline_results.json
8. pilot_pooled_metrics.json
9. pilot_zone_metrics.json
10. pilot_h4_decomposition.json
11. pilot_h5_metrics.json
12. pilot_paired_comparisons.json
13. pilot_power_analysis.json
14. pilot_validity_gates.json
15. pilot_summary_report.md
16. run_manifest.json

The manifest must include:

- run ID
- timestamp
- git commit
- configuration hash
- world registry hash
- scientific configuration
- exact world counts by zone
- exact boundary effect allocation
- artifact inventory
- hashes of scientific artifacts

============================================================
17. IMPLEMENTATION ISOLATION
============================================================

Prefer implementing the pilot in standalone files/directories.

Do not modify production pipelines.

Do not modify existing MLC v0.1 scientific semantics.

Reuse existing MLC components wherever possible.

If reuse requires changing existing scientific behavior:

STOP.

Write a specification issue report.

Do not silently patch the existing system.

============================================================
18. TEST REQUIREMENTS
============================================================

Add regression tests for at least:

1. exact 100-world registry,
2. exact zone composition,
3. correct boundary effect → ground truth mapping,
4. multiple seeds per boundary effect,
5. registry hash immutability,
6. threshold freeze and ordering,
7. pooled accuracy calculation,
8. Clear Zone accuracy,
9. Boundary Zone accuracy,
10. Evidence-Limited Zone accuracy,
11. H4 pooled catastrophic rate,
12. each H4 decomposition component,
13. H5 metrics,
14. paired MLC/B2 comparison,
15. paired MLC/B3 comparison,
16. n=500 power estimation,
17. required n for 80% power,
18. NO_DIFFERENCE vs INCONCLUSIVE support logic where applicable,
19. artifact completeness,
20. manifest generation,
21. forensic reconstruction from persisted artifacts.

Tests must include adversarial cases.

Do not only test happy paths.

============================================================
19. EXECUTION ORDER
============================================================

Follow this exact order:

A. inspect existing MLC implementation,

B. inspect existing scientific verdict evaluator,

C. inspect current configuration and detect specification conflicts,

D. implement pilot world generation,

E. freeze and hash world registry,

F. implement pilot validity gates,

G. implement pooled and zone-level metrics,

H. implement H4 decomposition,

I. implement pilot power analysis,

J. implement pilot artifacts and manifest,

K. add adversarial regression tests,

L. run tests,

M. execute the 100-world pilot,

N. run all pilot validity gates,

O. persist all artifacts,

P. generate the walkthrough report.

============================================================
20. STOP CONDITIONS
============================================================

STOP and report before execution if:

- existing code conflicts with this protocol,
- a frozen scientific threshold differs from this prompt,
- the 5pp minimum meaningful effect conflicts with another frozen specification,
- existing world-generation semantics cannot support the required boundary worlds without changing MLC scientific semantics,
- paired comparison records cannot be constructed cleanly,
- power estimation requires an unresolved scientific choice,
- any required artifact cannot be generated,
- any pilot validity gate definition is ambiguous.

Do not silently resolve scientific ambiguity.

============================================================
21. REQUIRED FINAL WALKTHROUGH
============================================================

After implementation and execution, provide:

A. Files created

B. Files modified

C. Whether any existing MLC scientific semantics changed

D. Exact pilot world allocation

E. Boundary effect → ground truth mapping

F. Seeds per boundary effect

G. Test results

H. Pilot validity gate results

I. Pooled MLC/B2/B3 performance

J. Clear Zone performance

K. Boundary Zone performance

L. Evidence-Limited Zone performance

M. H4 pooled catastrophic false admission results

N. H4 three-way decomposition

O. H5 results

P. H2 paired comparison and power analysis

Q. H3 paired comparison and power analysis

R. H4 paired comparison and power analysis

S. Estimated power at n=500 for H2/H3/H4

T. Estimated required n for 80% power for H2/H3/H4

U. Whether the planned 500-world primary experiment appears adequately powered

V. Artifact directory

W. Manifest summary

X. Specification issues found

Y. Highest-risk remaining scientific assumption

Z. Exact final pilot verdict

The final pilot verdict must be one of:

MLC_V0_1_PILOT_VALID_PRIMARY_DESIGN_ADEQUATELY_POWERED

MLC_V0_1_PILOT_VALID_PRIMARY_DESIGN_UNDERPOWERED

MLC_V0_1_PILOT_VALID_POWER_ESTIMATE_UNSTABLE

MLC_V0_1_PILOT_INVALID_WORLD_GENERATION

MLC_V0_1_PILOT_INVALID_COMPARISON_DESIGN

MLC_V0_1_PILOT_INVALID_IMPLEMENTATION

MLC_V0_1_PILOT_BLOCKED_BY_SPECIFICATION_CONFLICT

Do not create a different verdict.

============================================================
FINAL INSTRUCTION
============================================================

This pilot is not an attempt to prove that MLC works.

It is an attempt to determine whether the planned primary experiment is capable of producing a scientifically interpretable failure or success.

Preserve that distinction throughout implementation, analysis, artifacts, and reporting.

RELIANCE Empirical Anchoring Audit for S4-A
Objective

Perform a strictly read-only forensic empirical audit of the existing RELIANCE replay implementation, artifacts, and historical experiment outputs in dp-core-phase1-substrate-v3.

The purpose is to determine whether existing DP/EkamNet replay evidence can independently constrain any of the four mechanism parameters required for the future S4-A Selection Risk experiment:

Candidate Pool Size × True-Quality Distribution × Observation-Noise Structure × Selection Rule

This audit must also determine whether genuine simultaneous multi-candidate competition is currently a meaningful architectural phenomenon in DP/EkamNet at all.

This is an evidence-discovery audit.

It is not an implementation task.

It is not an S4-A design task.

It is not permission to manufacture plausible parameter values.

1. NON-NEGOTIABLE RULES
1.1 READ-ONLY

Do not modify any production code, experiment code, configuration, artifact, database, schema, test, or documentation.

Do not create fixes.

Do not refactor.

Do not add instrumentation.

Do not rerun experiments unless an existing command can be executed without changing code or configuration and execution is genuinely necessary to verify an audit claim.

Prefer existing artifacts and persisted data.

1.2 NO SYNTHETIC ANCHORING

Do not infer a numeric S4-A parameter merely because a plausible number would be useful.

Evidence must come from actual RELIANCE replay behavior, persisted artifacts, database records, logs, or executable code paths.

1.3 ABSENCE-OF-EVIDENCE FALLBACK RULE

If a parameter has:

Strength of Anchor = NONE

the audit must terminate that parameter's recommendation with:

UNSUPPORTED → EXPLORATORY GRID

Do not provide:

a fallback number,
a suggested placeholder,
an intuitively plausible value,
a "reasonable starting point,"
a numeric range inferred without replay evidence.

A missing anchor must remain missing.

1.4 DO NOT CONFUSE RECORD COUNT WITH COMPETITION

The existence of multiple:

hypotheses,
theories,
mechanisms,
experiences,
patterns,
lessons,
retrieved memories,

does not prove that multiple candidates were simultaneously competing for the same epistemic role.

The audit must distinguish:

record multiplicity

from:

genuine candidate competition

1.5 DO NOT CONFUSE TEMPORAL ACCUMULATION WITH CANDIDATE POOL SIZE

If four mechanisms existed across a 100-day replay but never simultaneously competed during one formation/selection event, the candidate pool size is not four.

1.6 NO RETROACTIVE S4-A DESIGN

Do not use the audit to design S4-A0.

Do not choose candidate-pool sizes.

Do not choose noise distributions.

Do not choose selection rules.

Do not propose implementation mechanics.

The audit may only state which future parameters are empirically anchored and which remain unsupported.

2. SCIENTIFIC CONTEXT

S4-A will eventually test:

Selection Risk × Winner's Curse / Retrospective Selection Optimism × Prospective Validation × Bounded Multi-Candidate Stationary Synthetic Environment

Before designing that experiment, we need to know whether historical DP/EkamNet replay behavior provides empirical constraints for its mechanism parameters.

The four target parameters are:

Candidate pool size.
True-quality distribution or an empirical proxy for candidate-quality dispersion.
Observation-noise structure or an empirical proxy for instability in candidate-quality estimates.
Selection rule.

The audit must additionally answer whether Selection Risk is currently:

ACTIVE / RARE / LATENT / NOT DETERMINABLE

in the existing DP/EkamNet architecture.

3. REQUIRED AUDIT SCOPE

Inspect all relevant existing code and evidence, including where available:

RELIANCE replay implementation;
replay orchestration;
hypothesis generation;
theory generation;
mechanism formation;
mechanism reuse;
mechanism mutation;
retirement and revival;
retrieval;

confidence evolution;
usefulness metrics;

existing tests;

hypothesis,

Trace actual semantics rather than relying only on class names.

# AG PROMPT — DP/EkamNet Epistemic Competition Reconciliation Audit

## Role

Act as a read-only forensic research auditor.

Your task is to determine whether the current or historical DP/EkamNet replay architecture contains evidence of genuine epistemic competition and selection among alternative theories, mechanisms, or principles.

This is a reconciliation audit only.

Do not:
- modify code,
- modify artifacts,
- create new experiments,
- create synthetic candidate pools,
- recommend S4-A parameters,
- redesign the roadmap,
- implement Exploration Risk experiments,
- infer missing evidence,
- treat absence of available artifacts as evidence of architectural absence.

The purpose is to establish the narrow empirical finding needed for a later human roadmap decision.

---

# 1. Required Claim Separation

The final report MUST keep these three claims separate:

1. EMPIRICAL FINDING

What does the inspected evidence establish about epistemic competition and selection in the current/historical replay architecture?

2. PARAMETER-ANCHORING CONSEQUENCE

Does the inspected evidence provide empirical anchors for S4-A parameters?

3. ROADMAP IMPLICATION

Do NOT decide whether Selection Risk or Exploration Risk should be tested next.

The roadmap implication must be reported as:

REQUIRES_HUMAN_ARCHITECTURAL_PRIORITY_DECISION

unless the audit discovers a specification contradiction requiring further investigation.

Do not allow roadmap recommendations to be presented as empirical audit findings.

---

# 2. Phase 0 — Artifact Availability Inventory

Before inspecting architectural behavior, determine exactly what evidence is available.

Search the repository and accessible artifact directories for:

- RELIANCE replay artifacts,
- 10-day replay artifacts,
- 30-day replay artifacts,
- 60-day replay artifacts,
- 90-day replay artifacts,
- 100-day replay artifacts,
- theory registries,
- theory lineage records,
- mechanism records,
- mechanism reuse records,
- principle records,
- principle reconciliation records,
- hierarchical merge records,
- lesson records,
- retirement records,
- revival records,
- mutation records,
- replay summaries,
- forensic reports,
- persisted databases or exports containing historical epistemic state.

For every relevant artifact found, report:

- exact path,
- artifact type,
- replay duration/date range if known,
- whether complete or partial,
- whether machine-readable,
- whether inspected,
- why it is relevant.

Explicitly answer:

WHAT_IS_THE_LONGEST_AVAILABLE_INSPECTABLE_RELIANCE_REPLAY?

Possible outcomes include:

- 100_DAY_AVAILABLE_AND_INSPECTED
- 90_DAY_AVAILABLE_AND_INSPECTED
- 60_DAY_AVAILABLE_AND_INSPECTED
- 30_DAY_AVAILABLE_AND_INSPECTED
- ONLY_SHORT_RUNS_AVAILABLE
- LONG_RUN_REFERENCED_BUT_ARTIFACTS_UNAVAILABLE
- INSUFFICIENT_EVIDENCE_TO_DETERMINE

Do not claim that long-run evidence was checked unless the underlying artifacts were actually found and inspected.

If historical reports mention a replay but its underlying artifacts are unavailable, distinguish:

HISTORICALLY_REFERENCED

from:

DIRECTLY_INSPECTED

---

# 3. Pre-Registered Operational Definition of Genuine Epistemic Competition

Freeze this definition before inspecting behavioral evidence.

A positive finding of GENUINE EPISTEMIC COMPETITION requires all of the following:

## Criterion 1 — Multiplicity

At least two distinct epistemic candidates exist simultaneously.

Candidates may be:

- theories,
- mechanisms,
- principles,
- or another explicitly represented epistemic object.

Historical versions of one lineage do not automatically count as multiple candidates.

---

## Criterion 2 — Shared Epistemic Role

The candidates address substantially the same epistemic question.

Examples include:

- explaining the same observation,
- predicting the same target,
- applying to the same trigger and regime,
- proposing incompatible mechanisms for the same phenomenon,
- competing for the same belief or representational role.

Candidates applying to unrelated conditions do not count.

---

## Criterion 3 — Meaningful Incompatibility or Substitutability

The candidates must differ in a way that creates a meaningful choice.

Examples:

- incompatible predictions,
- conflicting causal explanations,
- mutually inconsistent propositions,
- alternative mechanisms for the same effect,
- one candidate replacing or subordinating another.

Simple coexistence does not count.

Narrow and broad principles that can coexist without conflict do not automatically count.

---

## Criterion 4 — Comparative Process

The architecture must perform some operation that depends on the relationship between the candidates.

Examples:

- comparison,
- ranking,
- scoring relative to one another,
- reconciliation of conflict,
- preferential retention,
- selection,
- suppression,
- replacement,
- subordination,
- winner determination.

Independent evaluation of each candidate against a fixed threshold does not count as comparative selection.

---

## Criterion 5 — Selection Consequence

The comparative process must affect epistemic state.

Examples:

- one candidate survives and another is retired,
- one candidate is promoted over another,
- one candidate is selected for commitment,
- one claim is preserved while an incompatible claim is discarded,
- a merged representation preferentially preserves one candidate's semantics.

If all candidates remain independently represented with no preferential consequence, classify as coexistence rather than selection.

---

# 4. Explicit Non-Examples

The following MUST NOT automatically be classified as genuine epistemic competition:

- multiple historical versions of one evolving theory lineage,
- mutation of one theory into a later version,
- independent threshold-based retirement,
- independent usefulness scoring,
- multiple principles applying to different regimes,
- retrieval ranking for contextual relevance,
- mechanism reuse,
- principle consolidation that simply unions compatible statements,
- generalization from narrow principles into a broader compatible principle,
- chronological replacement without comparison,
- multiple active theories that address unrelated targets.

---

# 5. Classification Taxonomy

Every candidate event inspected must be classified as exactly one of:

1. NO_MULTIPLICITY

Only one epistemic candidate exists.

2. COEXISTENCE_NON_COMPETITIVE

Multiple candidates exist but serve different epistemic roles or do not meaningfully conflict.

3. INDEPENDENT_EVALUATION

Multiple candidates exist and are evaluated, but not comparatively.

4. IMPLICIT_COMPETITION

Candidates share an epistemic role, meaningfully conflict, and architecture behavior preferentially preserves, suppresses, replaces, or subordinates one candidate even without an explicit selection operator.

5. EXPLICIT_COMPETITION

Candidates are explicitly compared, ranked, or selected.

6. INSUFFICIENT_EVIDENCE

Artifacts or code do not permit reliable classification.

---

# 6. Required Longitudinal Analysis

Using the longest available inspectable RELIANCE replay, determine:

- maximum simultaneous active theory count,
- maximum simultaneous mechanism count where measurable,
- maximum simultaneous principle count,
- whether simultaneous objects address the same epistemic role,
- whether incompatible alternatives coexist,
- whether any object is selected relative to another,
- whether retirement is independent or comparative,
- whether mutation represents exploration or merely lineage evolution,
- whether revival introduces alternatives or restores a prior trajectory,
- whether mechanism reuse creates competition or only contextual reuse.

Do not infer competition from object counts alone.

For every claimed competition event, provide an exact causal trace.

---

# 7. Required Theory/Mechanism Analysis

Explicitly inspect whether:

- multiple active theories ever explain or predict the same target,
- multiple mechanisms ever compete to explain the same observed effect,
- theory mutation creates branching alternatives or replaces the parent trajectory,
- retired and active theories ever coexist as alternatives,
- revived theories compete with current theories,
- confidence evolution is independent or relative,
- usefulness scoring is independent or comparative.

Answer:

DOES_THE_THEORY_OR_MECHANISM_LAYER_CONTAIN_GENUINE_MULTI_CANDIDATE_COMPETITION?

Allowed answers:

YES_EXPLICIT

YES_IMPLICIT

NO_ONLY_COEXISTENCE

NO_ONLY_LINEAGE_EVOLUTION

INSUFFICIENT_EVIDENCE

---

# 8. Required Hierarchical Merge Inspection

Inspect the actual principle reconciliation and hierarchical merge implementation.

Determine:

- what inputs enter the merge,
- whether inputs can conflict,
- whether conflicts are detected,
- whether one principle can be preferred over another,
- whether one candidate's semantics can be discarded,
- whether merges preserve all compatible information,
- whether generalization occurs without competition,
- whether retirement occurs because of comparative judgment or independent thresholds.

Provide at least one exact code-path trace.

Answer:

DOES_HIERARCHICAL_MERGE_IMPLEMENT_IMPLICIT_EPISTEMIC_SELECTION?

Allowed answers:

YES

NO

PARTIALLY

INSUFFICIENT_EVIDENCE

Do not classify generalization or union as selection unless there is evidence of preferential preservation under meaningful incompatibility.

---

# 9. Candidate Pool Reconstruction

Attempt to reconstruct whether any historical replay event could satisfy the S4-A causal structure:

Multiple candidates
→ same W2 evidence opportunity
→ candidate-specific measurements
→ deterministic or implicit comparison
→ one candidate selected
→ selected candidate committed/evaluated

For each stage report:

- PRESENT
- ABSENT
- PARTIAL
- INSUFFICIENT_EVIDENCE

Then provide the exact implemented causal chain actually found.

---

# 10. S4-A Parameter Anchoring

Only after completing the empirical audit, answer whether replay evidence anchors:

- candidate pool size,
- true candidate quality dispersion,
- measurement noise,
- selection rule.

For each parameter report:

- evidence source,

- strength of anchor.

Strength values:

- STRONG
- MODERATE
- WEAK
- NONE

CRITICAL RULE:

If Strength of Anchor = NONE, terminate the parameter row with:

UNSUPPORTED → EXPLORATORY GRID

Do not suggest fallback numbers.

Do not suggest placeholder values.

Do not manufacture an empirical anchor.

---

# 11. Mandatory Distinction

The final report must explicitly distinguish between:

A. SELECTION_RISK_CHECKED_AND_FOUND_SMALL

and

B. SELECTION_RISK_NOT_YET_INSTANTIATED_IN_CURRENT_REPLAY_ARCHITECTURE

These are scientifically different findings.

Use B only if the architecture lacks the causal machinery required for genuine competition and selection.

Do not use terms such as:

- essentially nonexistent,
- negligible,

unless the risk was actually instantiated, measured, and found small.

---

---

For every major conclusion provide:

# AG PROMPT — S4-E0 PHASE 0 READ-ONLY ARCHITECTURE COMPATIBILITY AUDIT

## Context

We are working on DP/EkamNet and have completed the MLC v0.1 implementation, pilot, forensic audits, and subsequent Epistemic Safeguard Evaluation Methodology v0.1.

The MLC v0.1 pilot produced an important methodological lesson:

A safeguard can only be meaningfully evaluated in an environment whose causal structure actually contains the failure mechanism the safeguard is intended to address.

Subsequent audits of RELIANCE replay behavior found:

1. Multiple theories/mechanisms/principles may coexist.
2. Genuine simultaneous candidate competition for the same epistemic role was not established.
3. Selection Risk is therefore classified as:

   NOT_YET_INSTANTIATED_IN_CURRENT_REPLAY_ARCHITECTURE

4. Replay evidence does not empirically anchor S4-A candidate-pool parameters.
5. The roadmap decision was therefore made to investigate Exploration Risk before Selection Risk.
6. The next proposed experiment is S4-E0.

S4-E0 asks:

> Can DP create and preserve genuinely distinct explanatory alternatives for the same epistemic target, rather than merely producing paraphrases, parameter variants, or scope refinements?

Before designing or implementing S4-E0, we must determine whether the current DP/EkamNet architecture is compatible with such an experiment.

This task is therefore a strictly READ-ONLY Phase 0 Architecture Compatibility Audit.

---

# 1. PRIMARY OBJECTIVE

Determine whether the current DP/EkamNet architecture can support the scientific question posed by S4-E0 without modification.

Specifically determine:

A. Whether the current formation architecture can generate more than one candidate explanation for the same epistemic target.

B. Whether candidates are represented richly enough to distinguish genuinely different explanatory mechanisms from paraphrases, parameter variants, and scope refinements.

C. Whether multiple candidates can coexist long enough to be compared.

D. Whether the current architecture already contains any explicit or implicit explanatory-family representation.

E. Whether the current architecture already contains any explicit or implicit pairwise candidate comparison mechanism.

F. Whether the current architecture contains latent stochastic or procedural diversity sources that could affect a future bounded N-way formation extension.

G. Whether the proposed S4-E0 G1-G5 evaluation gates are executable against current architecture and persisted artifacts.

H. Whether a Minimal Formation Extension would be required before S4-E0 can run.

---

# 2. STRICT TASK BOUNDARY

This is a READ-ONLY audit.

DO NOT:

- modify production code;
- modify experiment code;
- create a formation extension;
- create multi-candidate generation;
- change prompts;
- change LLM parameters;
- change temperature;
- change sampling;
- change theory schemas;
- change mechanism schemas;
- change lifecycle states;
- add explanatory-family fields;
- implement G1-G5;
- generate synthetic candidate pools;
- execute S4-E0;
- recommend arbitrary candidate counts;
- recommend arbitrary temperatures;
- recommend arbitrary grid resolutions;
- invent parameter anchors;
- silently interpret missing capability as a defect;
- claim that DP lacks Exploration capability merely because S4-E0 cannot currently execute.

You may create a READ-ONLY audit script if necessary.

Any audit script must:

- inspect existing code/artifacts only;
- produce diagnostic output only;
- make zero scientific or production-state mutations.

---

# 3. SCIENTIFIC QUESTION

The scientific question motivating S4-E0 is:

> Can DP create and preserve genuinely distinct explanatory alternatives for the same epistemic target?

The experiment must NOT collapse this question into:

- Can an LLM generate multiple sentences?
- Can an LLM produce multiple hypotheses when explicitly prompted to be diverse?
- Can DP create parameter variants?
- Can DP create narrower or broader versions of the same explanation?
- Can DP create paraphrases?
- Can a synthetic stand-in generator manufacture candidate diversity?

The target capability is:

GENUINE EXPLANATORY PLURALITY

defined as:

Multiple candidate explanations concerning the same epistemic target and overlapping scope that encode meaningfully different explanatory structures and permit discriminating future observations.

---

# 4. FROZEN CONCEPTUAL DISTINCTIONS

The audit must preserve the following distinctions.

## 4.1 Candidate Multiplicity

More than one candidate exists.

This alone does NOT establish explanatory plurality.

---

## 4.2 Representational Diversity

Candidates differ in stored representation.

This may include:

- wording;
- thresholds;
- scopes;
- parameters;
- triggers;
- metadata.

This alone does NOT establish explanatory plurality.

---

## 4.3 Mechanistic Distinctness

Candidates encode genuinely different proposed explanatory structures.

Examples might include different:

- causal directions;
- drivers;
- mediators/processes;
- target effects.

This is stronger than representational diversity.

---

## 4.4 Epistemic Plurality

Candidates:

1. address the same epistemic target;
2. have overlapping scope;
3. encode meaningfully different explanatory mechanisms;
4. permit at least one constructable future observation within the overlapping scope where their predictions diverge.

This is the target phenomenon.

---

# 5. FAMILY ASSIGNMENT CLARIFICATION

The current S4-E0 design distinguishes:

A. Explanatory Family Assignment

from

B. Pairwise Mechanistic Distinctness Evaluation.

These MUST NOT be treated as identical operations.

Families organize explanatory space.

Alternatives may compete:

- across families; or
- within the same coarse explanatory family.

Therefore:

> G2/G3 pairwise evaluation eligibility is determined solely by shared epistemic target and overlapping scope.

Family assignment MUST NOT:

- gate candidate-pair eligibility;
- filter candidate pairs;
- reduce candidate pairs;
- determine in advance whether candidates are mechanistically distinct.

The audit must determine whether the current architecture could support this distinction.

---

# 6. PROVISIONAL S4-E0 GATES

The proposed S4-E0 evaluation structure is:

## G1 — Multiplicity

Are at least two candidate explanations present?

---

## G2 — Shared Epistemic Target + Overlapping Scope

Do at least two candidates address the same epistemic target and have overlapping applicability?

IMPORTANT:

All candidate pairs satisfying Target + Scope Overlap must remain eligible for G3 evaluation.

Family assignment must not gate pairwise evaluation.

---

## G3 — Mechanistic Distinctness

Do eligible candidates encode meaningfully different proposed mechanisms rather than:

- paraphrases;
- parameter variants;
- threshold variants;
- pure scope refinements?

---

## G4 — Constructable Discriminating Observation

Is there at least one constructable future observation inside the overlapping scope where candidate predictions differ?

The eventual G4 procedure must be mechanical and auditable.

The audit must determine whether current representations contain enough structure to support such a procedure.

DO NOT design or freeze arbitrary observation-grid resolution during this audit.

---

## G5 — Preservation

Can genuinely distinct alternatives coexist without premature merge, overwrite, retirement, mutation, or collapse before evaluation?

---

# 7. REQUIRED AUDIT QUESTIONS

Answer every question explicitly.

---

## Q1. Current Formation Cardinality

Trace the actual current hypothesis/theory formation path.

Determine:

- Does one formation event create exactly one candidate?
- Can one formation event create multiple candidates?
- Can multiple formation calls concerning the same epistemic target occur?
- If yes, are they preserved as separate candidates?
- Can they coexist simultaneously?
- Is there any explicit candidate-set abstraction?

Provide exact code-path evidence.

---

## Q2. Current Candidate Representation

Inspect the relevant schemas and persisted records.

Determine whether candidates currently encode structured fields corresponding to:

- epistemic target;
- trigger;
- scope;
- predicted outcome;
- causal direction;
- driver;
- mediator/process;
- target effect;
- confidence;
- provenance;
- lineage;
- formation source.

For every field classify:

- EXPLICITLY_STRUCTURED
- DERIVABLE
- FREE_TEXT_ONLY
- ABSENT

Do not infer structure that does not exist.

---

## Q3. Proposed Mechanism Representation

Determine whether current DP/EkamNet candidates possess a structured mechanism representation sufficient to distinguish:

- different wording;
- parameter variation;
- scope refinement;
- genuinely different explanatory mechanisms.

Answer:

CURRENTLY_SUFFICIENT

PARTIALLY_SUFFICIENT

INSUFFICIENT

Support the answer with code/schema/artifact evidence.

---

## Q4. Existing Family or Taxonomy Representation

Determine whether the architecture already contains anything equivalent or adjacent to:

- explanatory families;
- theory families;
- mechanism families;
- lineage families;
- abstraction categories;
- principle hierarchies.

For each discovered construct determine:

1. what it actually represents;
2. how membership is assigned;
3. whether assignment is structural, deterministic, LLM-mediated, or heuristic;
4. whether it could legitimately support S4-E0 explanatory-family assignment;
5. whether reusing it would conflate lineage, similarity, abstraction, or explanation.

Do not treat similarly named concepts as equivalent without evidence.

---

## Q5. Candidate Coexistence and Preservation

Trace candidate lifecycle behavior.

Determine whether multiple candidates addressing the same target can:

- coexist;
- persist independently;
- accumulate evidence independently;
- retain independent provenance;
- avoid automatic merge;
- avoid automatic mutation into one lineage;
- avoid premature retirement;
- survive until comparison.

Identify every architecture mechanism that could collapse plurality before G5 can evaluate it.

---

## Q6. Existing Comparison or Selection Mechanisms

Search for all mechanisms involving:

- ranking;
- max;
- argmax;
- top-k;
- similarity sorting;
- best match;
- reconciliation;
- merging;
- retirement;
- dominance;
- confidence comparison;
- usefulness comparison.

For every mechanism found determine whether it represents:

A. epistemic candidate competition;

B. lineage-parent selection;

C. retrieval selection;

D. resource prioritization;

E. reconciliation/generalization;

F. something else.

Do not classify every ranking operation as epistemic selection.

---

## Q7. Latent Diversity Sources in Current Formation

This question is mandatory.

Inspect the current single-candidate formation pathway for any source of stochastic or procedural diversity.

Check explicitly for:

- LLM temperature;
- top-p;
- top-k sampling;
- random seeds;
- nondeterministic model calls;
- retries;
- repeated LLM calls;
- multiple prompts;
- different context framings;
- deterministic search;
- LLM discovery;
- residual discovery;
- fallback generation;
- prompt variation;
- context variation;
- model variation;
- asynchronous ordering effects;
- any other source capable of producing different candidate outputs from equivalent input.

For every source found report:

1. source;
2. exact code path;
3. whether it is intentional;
4. whether it is deterministic;
5. whether repeated formation calls could produce distinct outputs;
6. whether a future bounded N-way wrapper would inherit this diversity source.

This question is critical because a future Minimal Formation Extension must not be incorrectly described as neutral if the existing formation pathway already contains diversity-producing mechanisms.

---

# 17. IMPORTANT INTERPRETATION RULES

The audit must preserve these distinctions:

1. No candidate multiplicity does not prove DP lacks creativity.

2. Multiple generated texts do not prove explanatory plurality.

3. Multiple candidates do not prove mechanistic distinctness.

4. Mechanistic distinctness does not prove discriminating observations exist.

5. Family diversity does not prove epistemic plurality.

6. Same-family candidates may still be genuine epistemic alternatives.

7. Family assignment must never gate pairwise target/scope evaluation.

8. Existing stochasticity does not automatically imply useful exploration.

9. Lack of structured mechanism representation is an architectural finding, not an implementation bug.

10. Need for a Minimal Formation Extension changes the scientific unit being evaluated.

11. S4-E0 must not be executed until the architecture compatibility question is resolved.

12. Missing empirical anchors must not be replaced with convenient numeric defaults.

13. Absence of evidence is an acceptable audit result.

14. The audit must not recommend roadmap priority between Selection Risk and Exploration Risk.

15. The audit reports evidence. Roadmap decisions remain human decisions.

# AG PROMPT — Proposition Extension & Formation Boundary Protocol v0.1

You are working in the DP/EkamNet repository.

Your task is to perform a READ-ONLY architecture falsification audit.

DO NOT modify code.
DO NOT create implementation code.
DO NOT refactor schemas.
DO NOT add Proposition fields.
DO NOT modify the MLC lifecycle.
DO NOT modify ERC behavior.
DO NOT implement Theory→Proposition transformation.
DO NOT implement alternative_group_id.
DO NOT recommend implementation work automatically from the audit result.

This task exists to test whether the current architectural hypothesis survives contact with the actual repository.

===============================================================================
1. CONTEXT
===============================================================================

DP/EkamNet is investigating how domain-specific hypothesis formation should hand off to the domain-independent epistemic substrate.

The current architectural hypothesis is:

H0:

Existing Proposition is sufficient as the atomic domain-independent
representation of an epistemic alternative, provided it is minimally extended
with structured explanatory semantics and provisional sibling-group membership.

The competing hypothesis is:

H1:

Representing epistemic alternatives as extended Propositions creates
unacceptable semantic, lifecycle, relationship, integration, or resource
distortion, requiring a distinct representation boundary or primitive.

IMPORTANT:

The purpose of this audit is NOT to justify H0.

The purpose is to attempt to falsify H0.

Narrative elegance is not evidence.

The architectural story:

    Theory → Proposition → Compilation → Evidence → Measurement → Belief

must not be accepted merely because it appears conceptually clean.

It must be tested against the actual repository.

===============================================================================
2. SCIENTIFIC UNIT OF EVALUATION
===============================================================================

The canonical audit result is NOT a single verdict.

The canonical result is the structured tuple:

SemanticFitResult
× LifecycleFitResult
× RelationshipFitResult
× TheoryIntegrationFitResult
× ResourceFitResult

Each dimension must independently receive exactly one status:

SUPPORTED
STRAINED
INCOMPATIBLE
NOT_INTERPRETABLE

Definitions:

SUPPORTED
    Existing architecture can accommodate the proposed extension without
    material semantic distortion, lifecycle reinterpretation, hidden coupling,
    or invariant violation.

STRAINED
    Accommodation appears possible, but requires meaningful architectural
    friction, special cases, additional semantics, or changes that weaken the
    claim that this is a genuinely minimal extension.

INCOMPATIBLE
    The proposed extension conflicts with existing architecture sufficiently
    that H0 does not survive on this dimension.

NOT_INTERPRETABLE
    Repository evidence is insufficient to make a defensible determination.

Do not collapse these statuses into a single atomic scientific record.

A derived summary label may be reported, but only after all five canonical
dimension results are preserved independently.

===============================================================================

===============================================================================

The final report must explicitly separate:

A. EMPIRICAL / CODE FINDINGS

What the repository actually demonstrates.

B. ARCHITECTURAL CONSEQUENCES

What follows directly from those findings.

C. ROADMAP DECISIONS

Human decisions about what should be built next.

The auditor may report A and B.

The auditor MUST NOT silently convert A or B into C.

If implementation choices remain, report:

    HUMAN_ARCHITECTURAL_DECISION_REQUIRED

Do not automatically recommend:

- extending Proposition,
- creating a new primitive,
- modifying Theory,
- changing ERC,
- modifying MLC,
- or implementing S4-E0.

4. AUDIT QUESTION 1 — SEMANTIC FIT
===============================================================================

Question:

Can Proposition absorb the semantics required for an epistemic alternative
while retaining one coherent meaning throughout the EkamNet lifecycle?

The proposed conceptual extension may eventually require fields equivalent to:

- target
- scope
- proposed_mechanism
- prediction semantics
- provenance
- formation source
- provisional alternative_group_id

DO NOT add these fields.

Inspect the existing Proposition schema and all significant Proposition usage.

Determine:

1. What does Proposition currently mean?

2. Which fields currently define its semantics?

3. Which components read Proposition?

4. Which components write or mutate Proposition?

5. Does Proposition maintain one coherent semantic meaning across:

   - creation
   - compilation
   - evidence accumulation
   - freezing
   - prospective validation
   - decision
   - belief-memory persistence

6. Would the proposed explanatory fields remain meaningful throughout the
   lifecycle?

7. Would some fields exist only for pre-compilation formation and become dead
   semantic baggage afterward?

8. Would existing code need repeated branching to determine what "kind" of
   Proposition it is?

9. Would formation source or sibling membership alter the meaning of existing
   Proposition fields?

10. Are there already multiple implicit Proposition subtypes hidden inside the
    current schema?

H0 is weakened or falsified on Semantic Fit if repository evidence suggests:

- mutually incompatible Proposition meanings,
- substantial mode/type branching would be required,
- explanatory semantics become meaningless after compilation,
- existing fields acquire different meanings depending on formation source,
- sibling membership changes what Proposition fundamentally represents,
- or the extension effectively creates a new primitive while merely retaining
  the Proposition class name.

1. Proposition can remain the atomic node.
2. sibling/group metadata can be a minimal provisional extension.
3. pairwise comparison can remain external and stateless for S4-E0.
4. persistent epistemic relationships are a possible future requirement but are NOT an S4-E0 requirement.
5. the current major unresolved formation-boundary decision is:

   Strategy A:
   Current Theory output
       →
   post-hoc Theory → structured Proposition adapter

   versus

   Strategy B:
   Current formation context
       →
   direct structured Proposition-compatible output

However, two questions remain unresolved:

A. ERC RESOURCE SCOPE

The prior audit showed that N sibling propositions do not incur a sibling-specific cost relative to N unrelated propositions.

It did NOT conclusively establish whether ERC budgets are scoped:

- globally per experiment/run,
- per replay,
- per world,
- per target,
- per proposition,
- per lifecycle,
- or through some other reset/allocation boundary.

Therefore aggregate cross-group starvation remains unresolved.

B. FORMATION BOUNDARY FEASIBILITY

The architectural narrative favoring Strategy B is persuasive but is not evidence.

Direct structured formation does not eliminate LLM non-determinism.

It relocates non-determinism from post-hoc translation to initial structured generation.

The unresolved question is:

Can DP’s act of explanation be converted into EkamNet’s unit of evaluation without silently changing what was explained?

- separate ERC instances,

- target-level accounting,

5. CENTRAL DIAGNOSTIC QUESTION
===============================================================================

Can the smallest architecturally plausible modification of current DP formation emit one structured explanatory candidate that is:

1. schema-valid,
2. semantically faithful to the formation context,
3. source-traceable,
4. auditable,
5. compatible with current Compilation assumptions,

without silently inventing, deleting, or materially changing the explanation?

===============================================================================
6. STRATEGIES TO CHARACTERIZE
===============================================================================

STRATEGY A — POST-HOC ADAPTER

Current DP formation
→
existing Theory output
→
frozen Theory→Proposition transformation
→
structured Proposition-compatible candidate

STRATEGY B — DIRECT STRUCTURED FORMATION

Current DP formation context
→
frozen structured-formation procedure
→
structured Proposition-compatible candidate

The diagnostic must NOT assume either strategy is superior.

The diagnostic must be capable of concluding:

- Strategy A is more feasible,
- Strategy B is more feasible,
- both are feasible with different costs,
- neither is currently feasible,
- evidence is inconclusive.

===============================================================================
7. REPRESENTATION BOUNDARY
===============================================================================

Use the smallest Proposition-compatible extension currently required by S4-E0.

At minimum consider whether the diagnostic candidate requires:

- proposition_id,
- source_theory_id or source formation provenance,
- target_definition,
- trigger_definition,
- scope_definition,
- proposed_mechanism,
- alternative_group_id OPTIONAL/NULL for this diagnostic,
- provenance references.

ProposedMechanism must remain structured.

At minimum evaluate the need for fields equivalent to:

- mechanism_type,
- causal_direction,
- driver,
- mediator_or_process,
- target_effect.

Do NOT automatically declare all fields mandatory.

The diagnostic design must determine:

1. which fields already exist semantically in current Theory output,
2. which exist only as free text,
3. which are absent,
4. which would require LLM inference,
5. which can be deterministically derived,
6. which cannot currently be grounded.

===============================================================================
8. FORMATION BOUNDARY INDEPENDENCE INVARIANT
===============================================================================

The diagnostic must freeze Strategy A and Strategy B procedures BEFORE diagnostic outputs are inspected.

Neither procedure may be iteratively modified to improve:

- schema validity,
- semantic fidelity,
- source traceability,
- apparent explanatory quality,
- agreement with human reviewers.

Parameter/procedure justification hierarchy:

1. empirical evidence from current DP formation behavior,
2. existing architectural intent,
3. established convention,
4. explicit characterization grid.

If none exists:

classify the parameter/procedure as:

UNSUPPORTED_REQUIRES_CHARACTERIZATION

Do NOT invent a convenient default number, prompt, threshold, or transformation rule.

===============================================================================
9. REQUIRED COMPARABILITY INVARIANT
===============================================================================

Strategy A and Strategy B must receive equivalent source information.

The diagnostic design must explicitly specify how this is guaranteed.

At minimum:

- same observation context,
- same market/world state,
- same historical evidence availability,
- same target phenomenon,
- same source data cutoff.

The only intended difference is the formation boundary:

A:
free-form Theory first, structured conversion second.

B:
structured Proposition-compatible generation directly.

If equivalent information exposure cannot be guaranteed, the diagnostic must classify the comparison as confounded.

===============================================================================
10. SOURCE-TRACEABILITY REQUIREMENT
===============================================================================

Every structured output field must be classified as one of:

DIRECTLY_PRESENT_IN_SOURCE

DETERMINISTICALLY_DERIVED

UNSUPPORTED_OR_INVENTED

For Strategy A:

“source” means the original Theory plus the formation context available to the adapter, depending on the frozen adapter design.

For Strategy B:

“source” means the frozen formation context provided to the structured-generation procedure.

strategy

===============================================================================
11. SEMANTIC FIDELITY
===============================================================================

The diagnostic must operationalize semantic fidelity.

Do NOT use:

“looks equivalent”

“seems faithful”

“same meaning”

as sufficient criteria.

Design an auditable procedure.

At minimum distinguish:

A. INFORMATION PRESERVATION

Did the structured candidate preserve explanatory information present in the source?

B. INFORMATION DELETION

Did material explanatory information disappear?

C. INFORMATION INVENTION

Did the structured candidate introduce claims unsupported by source context?

D. INFORMATION DISTORTION

Did the structured representation materially alter causal direction, scope, target, trigger, or mechanism?

Specify:

- automated checks where possible,
- deterministic structural checks,
- optional blinded human diagnostic review,
- limitations of each method.

===============================================================================
12. SCHEMA VALIDITY
===============================================================================

Specify exact schema-validity checks.

At minimum:

- parseability,
- required-field presence,
- enum validity where applicable,
- type validity,
- deterministic normalization,
- forbidden nulls if any,
- provenance completeness.

Schema validity alone MUST NOT count as semantic success.

A candidate can be:

SCHEMA_VALID_BUT_SEMANTICALLY_UNGROUNDED

This must be a legitimate outcome.

===============================================================================
13. COMPILATION COMPATIBILITY
===============================================================================

Trace current Compilation assumptions and design a compatibility check.

Ask:

1. Can the structured candidate enter current Compilation unchanged?

2. Does Compilation require fields not produced by the boundary strategy?

3. Does the strategy bypass existing specificity checks?

4. Does the strategy bypass tautology checks?

5. Does the strategy bypass contradiction pre-registration?

6. Does direct structured formation accidentally perform work that belongs inside Compilation?

This is critical.

Strategy B must NOT “succeed” by quietly moving Compilation logic upstream into the formation prompt.

→

→
structured Proposition-compatible candidate

The relevant question is:

Which strategy makes semantic transformation more observable, auditable, and falsifiable?

15. DIAGNOSTIC CASE SELECTION
===============================================================================

Design a case-selection procedure.

Do not choose only convenient examples.

Cases should cover, where available:

- simple Theory with explicit trigger/target/mechanism,

- Theory with ambiguous scope,
- Theory with missing causal direction,
- Theory containing free-text explanation not cleanly representable in current Proposition fields,

classify:

CASE_TAXONOMY_UNSUPPORTED_REQUIRES_CHARACTERIZATION

Do not manufacture frequencies.

===============================================================================
16. HUMAN REVIEW
===============================================================================

Human review may be used only as a blinded diagnostic.

It must not silently become the ground-truth engine.

Design must specify:

- what is blinded,
- what reviewers see,
- what they do not see,
- sampling procedure,
- disagreement handling,
- whether review compares A/B outputs,
- how automation-vs-human disagreement is preserved.

Do not choose arbitrary sample size if diagnostic volume is not yet known.

Freeze the sampling PRINCIPLE now.

Freeze exact n only after expected diagnostic volume is established and before outputs are inspected.

Per the frozen Epistemic Safeguard Evaluation Methodology:

benefit alone is insufficient.

19. PRE-REGISTERED INTERPRETATIONS
===============================================================================

Before execution, define what each broad result means.

At minimum:

A. Strategy A schema-valid + faithful, Strategy B not

Interpretation:
Current Theory representation can support a post-hoc boundary adapter more reliably than direct structured formation under the tested environment.

B. Strategy B schema-valid + faithful, Strategy A not

Interpretation:
Direct structured formation is more feasible under the tested environment.

Do NOT conclude:
“Strategy B is universally superior.”

C. Both succeed

Interpretation:
Architectural decision should be based on measured cost, auditability, coupling, and downstream compatibility.

D. Both fail

Interpretation:
Current Proposition extension or current formation representation may be insufficient.

Do not immediately create a new cognitive primitive.

E. CI/uncertainty insufficient to distinguish

Interpretation:
INCONCLUSIVE.

Do not force an architectural decision.

===============================================================================
20. PROPOSITION EXTENSION H₀ FALSIFICATION
===============================================================================

State exactly what diagnostic evidence could falsify:

H₀:
Proposition remains a sufficient atomic node.

Potential falsification requires evidence that the structured explanatory candidate cannot be represented without changing what Proposition fundamentally IS.

Examples that do NOT automatically falsify H₀:

- need for a better prompt,
- need for an adapter,
- need for external provenance,
- need for group metadata,
- need for pairwise harness logic,
- need for persistent relationships later,
- higher ERC cost,
- schema-validation failures caused by implementation defects.

Examples that MAY falsify H₀:

- essential explanatory semantics cannot be represented without turning Proposition into a fundamentally different object,
- the atomic node must simultaneously encode mutually incompatible explanations,
- lifecycle semantics become incoherent because one Proposition must internally represent multiple competing candidates,
- Compilation cannot operate without fundamentally changing Proposition identity or meaning.

PRESERVED:
Output meaning is supported by source and causal direction is unchanged.

DELETED:
Source contains materially relevant information absent from output.

INVENTED:
Output contains materially relevant information unsupported by source.

DISTORTED:
Output changes causal direction, target, scope, mechanism, or contradiction semantics.

INDETERMINATE:
Available source/output evidence cannot support a reliable classification.

Do not collapse these atomic findings into a fidelity float before analysis.

If an aggregate score is later derived, it must remain secondary to the atomic record.

# AG RESEARCH PROMPT

## DP / EKAMNET — FORMATION BOUNDARY DIAGNOSTIC PHASE 0

### TASK: DESIGN THE READ-ONLY SEMANTIC FIDELITY DIAGNOSTIC PROTOCOL

You are continuing the DP/EkamNet research program from the authoritative research handoff provided in the current context.

Treat that handoff as frozen research state.

Do not reconstruct the prior conversation.

Do not reopen closed research phases unless new direct evidence requires it.

The governing architectural principle remains:

DP MAY IMAGINE FREELY.

EKAMNET MAY BELIEVE ONLY THROUGH EVIDENCE.

The current research frontier is:

THEORY
→
FORMATION HANDOFF
→
PROPOSITION

The current governing architectural hypothesis is:

PROPOSITION_EXTENSION_HYPOTHESIS_STRAINED_BUT_NOT_FALSIFIED

The immediate research phase is:

FORMATION BOUNDARY DIAGNOSTIC PHASE 0

Your task is to design the smallest scientifically defensible read-only diagnostic protocol capable of characterizing the semantic boundary between current DP Theory artifacts and the frozen Proposition-compatible semantic schema.

DO NOT IMPLEMENT THE DIAGNOSTIC.

DO NOT MODIFY PRODUCTION CODE.

DO NOT EXECUTE THE DIAGNOSTIC.

DO NOT SELECT STRATEGY A OR STRATEGY B.

This task is protocol design only.

======================================================================

1. GOVERNING SCIENTIFIC QUESTION
   ======================================================================

Design a diagnostic capable of answering:

CAN THE EXPLICIT SEMANTIC CONTENT OF REPRESENTATIVE CURRENT DP THEORY ARTIFACTS BE REPRESENTED WITHIN THE FROZEN PROPOSITION-COMPATIBLE SEMANTIC SCHEMA WITHOUT MATERIAL:

* deletion;
* invention;
* distortion;
* hidden reasoning dependency;
* or residual loss of epistemically relevant source meaning?

The diagnostic must characterize where any semantic gap resides.

It must distinguish among at least:

1. SOURCE UNDER-SPECIFICATION

Current Theory does not explicitly contain semantic information required by the frozen Proposition-compatible schema.

2. TRANSLATIONAL INVENTION

Populating a structured field would require reasoning or semantic content not explicitly supported by the source Theory.

3. TRANSLATIONAL DISTORTION

The structured representation changes or materially weakens the meaning present in the source Theory.

4. TARGET SCHEMA LOSS

The Theory contains epistemically relevant meaning for which the frozen Proposition-compatible semantic schema provides no adequate representation.

These mechanisms must not be conflated.

======================================================================
2. PRIMARY RESEARCH SCOPE
=========================

Phase 0 is a SOURCE-TO-TARGET SEMANTIC REPRESENTABILITY DIAGNOSTIC.

It is NOT yet a Strategy A versus Strategy B experiment.

The diagnostic must operate on representative existing Theory artifacts.

It must determine:

A. whether the explicit semantics of current Theory artifacts can faithfully populate the frozen semantic fields;

and

B. whether epistemically relevant Theory meaning exists outside those fields and would therefore be lost at the boundary.

The diagnostic must examine both directions:

SOURCE → TARGET FIELD REPRESENTABILITY

and

SOURCE → TARGET SCHEMA COVERAGE

Do not design a one-directional diagnostic that asks only whether the expected Proposition fields can be populated.

Such a diagnostic would be destination-biased.

======================================================================
3. FROZEN SEMANTIC FIELDS
=========================

The diagnostic must evaluate the following ten frozen semantic fields:

1. trigger_definition

2. target_definition

3. scope_definition

4. expected_direction

5. contradiction_definition

6. mechanism_type

7. causal_direction

8. driver

9. mediator_or_process

10. target_effect

Use the frozen Atomic Field-Level Fidelity Schema.

Allowed fidelity classifications are:

PRESERVED

DELETED

INVENTED

DISTORTED

UNSUPPORTED_IN_SOURCE

NOT_APPLICABLE

INDETERMINATE

Allowed uncertainty levels are:

HIGH

MEDIUM

LOW

UNMEASURED

The diagnostic protocol must preserve:

* source evidence;
* source location;
* source explicit value;
* output or interpreted field value;
* comparison rule and version;
* classification;
* rationale;
* confidence / uncertainty;
* automated vs human reviewer;
* reviewer identity;
* adjudication status;
* provenance;
* artifact hashes.

Do not silently modify the frozen schema.

If the existing schema proves insufficient for recording a Phase 0 observation, report that as a finding or protocol limitation rather than changing it.

======================================================================
4. CRITICAL INTERPRETATION INVARIANT
====================================

A Phase 0 failure does NOT automatically falsify Proposition H₀.

The governing Proposition hypothesis remains:

H₀:

PROPOSITION IS A SUFFICIENT ATOMIC NODE FOR REPRESENTING S4-E0 EPISTEMIC ALTERNATIVES.

The following possible findings must remain separated:

A. Theory lacks explicit semantic information.

B. Translation requires unsupported reasoning.

C. Translation distorts existing meaning.

D. The frozen target schema cannot represent important Theory meaning.

E. Proposition itself is fundamentally the wrong atomic object.

Only evidence requiring a change to what Proposition fundamentally IS may falsify Proposition H₀.

Do not convert source insufficiency, adapter difficulty, extraction difficulty, execution architecture, or external relationship requirements into evidence against Proposition H₀.

======================================================================
5. REQUIRED PROTOCOL COMPONENTS
===============================

Design the smallest defensible protocol containing at least the following components.

---

## 5.1 ARTIFACT SAMPLING RULE

Define how representative current Theory artifacts should be selected.

The sampling procedure must be frozen before semantic inspection.

Prevent cherry-picking.

Prevent selection based on:

* apparent Theory quality;
* verbosity;
* compatibility with the ten fields;
* expected diagnostic success or failure.

Determine:

* the minimum defensible sample size;
* the source replay(s) or artifact population;
* inclusion criteria;
* exclusion criteria;
* deterministic sampling procedure;
* whether stratification is scientifically necessary.

Prefer the smallest sample capable of revealing systematic boundary behavior.

Do not maximize sample size merely for apparent rigor.

Explain why the proposed sample is sufficient for a diagnostic phase.

---

## 5.2 UNIT OF ANALYSIS

Define the exact scientific unit of analysis.

Determine whether it is:

* Theory artifact;
* Theory version;
* Theory × semantic field;
* explicit semantic claim;
* or another unit.

If multiple units are required, distinguish:

PRIMARY UNIT

SECONDARY UNIT

AGGREGATION UNIT

Do not leave the unit of analysis implicit.

---

## 5.3 SOURCE SEMANTIC INVENTORY PROCEDURE

Design a frozen procedure for identifying the explicit epistemically relevant semantic content of each Theory artifact.

This procedure must occur independently of the ten-field target assessment to the greatest practical extent.

Its purpose is to establish what meaning exists in the source before asking whether the destination can represent it.

Define:

* what counts as explicit source meaning;
* what counts as reasonable normalization;
* what counts as interpretation;
* what counts as additional reasoning;
* how source spans are recorded;
* how ambiguous meaning is handled;
* how compound claims are decomposed;
* how reviewer inference is constrained.

The procedure must not manufacture semantics merely because a target field expects them.

---

## 5.4 TEN-FIELD REPRESENTABILITY ASSESSMENT

Design the procedure for evaluating each Theory against each of the ten frozen fields.

For every Theory × field pair, determine the applicable frozen classification.

Explicitly define operational decision rules for:

PRESERVED

DELETED

INVENTED

DISTORTED

UNSUPPORTED_IN_SOURCE

NOT_APPLICABLE

INDETERMINATE

Pay particular attention to the distinction between:

UNSUPPORTED_IN_SOURCE

and

NOT_APPLICABLE.

Prevent reviewers from treating every absent field as a Theory defect.

Prevent reviewers from inferring values merely because they appear obvious.

---

## 5.5 HIDDEN REASONING DEPENDENCY TEST

Design a procedure for detecting whether populating a target field requires an additional reasoning layer.

For every field considered representable, ask:

CAN THIS VALUE BE DERIVED FROM EXPLICIT SOURCE INFORMATION USING ONLY THE PRE-REGISTERED COMPARISON OR NORMALIZATION RULE?

OR:

DOES POPULATING THIS FIELD REQUIRE NEW EXPLANATORY, CAUSAL, DOMAIN, OR INTERPRETIVE REASONING?

Define an operational classification scheme.

At minimum distinguish:

DIRECTLY_SUPPORTED

NORMALIZATION_ONLY

REASONING_DEPENDENT

INDETERMINATE

Explain whether REASONING_DEPENDENT should be represented through the existing fidelity schema, an orthogonal diagnostic field, or another non-destructive mechanism.

Do not silently alter the frozen fidelity classifications.

---

## 5.6 RESIDUAL SEMANTIC LOSS TEST

Design a procedure that asks:

DOES THE SOURCE THEORY CONTAIN EPISTEMICALLY RELEVANT MEANING THAT CANNOT BE ADEQUATELY REPRESENTED BY ANY OF THE TEN FROZEN FIELDS?

This test is mandatory.

It must protect against destination bias.

Define:

* what counts as epistemically relevant residual meaning;
* how residuals are identified;
* how residuals are recorded;
* how trivial prose differences are excluded;
* how duplicate semantic content is handled;
* how uncertainty is represented.

Do not assume the ten fields are a complete semantic model merely because they are frozen.

---

## 5.7 BLIND REVERSE-COVERAGE TEST

Design the smallest feasible independent reverse-coverage test.

An evaluator should inspect the original Theory artifact without using the ten fields as the primary search frame and identify:

EPISTEMICALLY IMPORTANT MEANING THAT WOULD BE LOST IF THE ORIGINAL THEORY WERE REPLACED ENTIRELY BY ITS TEN-FIELD STRUCTURED REPRESENTATION.

Determine:

* whether the reviewer must be fully blind to the target schema;
* what practical degree of independence is feasible;
* how reverse-coverage findings are compared with residual-loss findings;
* what disagreement means;
* whether this requires a second reviewer or can be performed through temporally separated review.

Prefer methodological independence over procedural complexity.

---

## 5.8 REVIEWER MODEL

Define the minimum defensible reviewer architecture.

Determine:

* automated reviewer role;
* human reviewer role;
* whether independent dual review is necessary;
* what subset, if any, requires human review;
* adjudication procedure;
* reviewer disagreement measurement;
* whether reviewers should be blinded to architectural hypotheses or desired outcomes.

Do not create unnecessary reviewer complexity.

However, do not allow a single evaluator to silently become:

* source interpreter;
* target mapper;
* residual-loss judge;
* and final adjudicator

if doing so creates unacceptable circularity.

---

## 5.9 COMPARISON RULE FREEZE

Define exactly what must be frozen before execution.

At minimum consider:

* artifact sampling rule;
* source semantic inventory procedure;
* field mapping rules;
* normalization rules;
* fidelity classification rules;
* hidden reasoning dependency rules;
* residual semantic loss rules;
* reverse-coverage procedure;
* reviewer prompts if LLM reviewers are used;
* model and version;
* temperature and seed where applicable;
* adjudication rules;
* aggregation rules;
* outcome thresholds.

Identify which elements are experimental levers.

Explain how post-inspection tuning will be prevented.

---

## 5.10 AGGREGATION RULES

Define how atomic findings should be aggregated without hiding important failure modes.

Do not rely only on a single pooled fidelity score.

At minimum preserve decomposition by:

* semantic field;
* Theory artifact;
* failure mechanism;
* fidelity classification;
* hidden reasoning dependency;
* residual semantic loss.

Determine the smallest useful summary metrics.

Avoid metric proliferation.

Explain why each proposed metric is scientifically necessary.

======================================================================

=============================

NEGATIVE

INCONCLUSIVE

* and adequate power.

Do not invent a comparison merely to preserve the four-label structure.

## 6.1 POSITIVE

The intended conceptual meaning is:

Representative current Theory artifacts demonstrate adequate semantic representability within the frozen Proposition-compatible schema, with acceptably low deletion, invention, distortion, hidden reasoning dependency, and residual semantic loss under the pre-registered diagnostic procedure.

Define the exact evidence required.

* Strategy A works;
* Strategy B works;
* Proposition is validated;
* S4-E0 is ready;
* the formation architecture is solved.

## 6.2 NEGATIVE

The intended conceptual meaning is:

The diagnostic demonstrates systematic semantic incompatibility exceeding pre-registered failure thresholds.

NEGATIVE findings must be decomposed by causal subtype.

At minimum consider:

SOURCE_INSUFFICIENCY

TRANSLATION_DEPENDENCY

TRANSLATION_DISTORTION

REPRESENTATION_INSUFFICIENCY

MIXED_FAILURE

Determine whether these are sufficient and mutually interpretable.

Do not allow a pooled NEGATIVE result to hide the location of the failure.

---

## 6.3 INCONCLUSIVE

The intended conceptual meaning is:

The evidence is insufficient to determine whether the current Theory → Proposition semantic boundary is adequately faithful or systematically deficient.

Define exact conditions capable of producing INCONCLUSIVE.

At minimum consider:

* insufficient representative artifacts;
* excessive INDETERMINATE findings;
* unacceptable reviewer disagreement;
* ambiguous source semantics;
* inability to distinguish source insufficiency from target schema insufficiency.

Do not collapse INCONCLUSIVE into NO_DIFFERENCE.
