7. REQUIRED CAUSAL GATES
========================

Apply the frozen Epistemic Safeguard Evaluation Methodology where relevant.

Does the selected Theory artifact population actually instantiate the possibility of semantic handoff failure?

ISOLATION GATE

Can the diagnostic distinguish among:

* poor source Theory quality;
* source under-specification;
* translation difficulty;

* schema expectancy effects;
* excessive inference;
* artifact selection bias;
* metric-induced distortion?

8. REQUIRED ADVERSARIAL TESTS
=============================

Design the minimum set of adversarial protocol tests required before diagnostic execution.

At minimum test whether the protocol can correctly handle:

1. a Theory that explicitly supports nearly all ten fields;

2. a Theory that is semantically meaningful but supports very few target fields;

3. a Theory where a target field appears obvious but is not explicitly supported;

4. a Theory containing important meaning outside the ten-field schema;

5. a Theory containing ambiguous or contradictory source text;

6. a case where normalization is valid;

7. a case where additional reasoning would be required;

8. a case where UNSUPPORTED_IN_SOURCE and NOT_APPLICABLE could easily be confused.

For each adversarial case define the expected protocol behavior.

Do not tune the protocol merely until the adversarial cases pass.

If an adversarial test exposes a conceptual defect, report the defect.

=======================

* architectural elegance;

* producing a positive verdict.

* falsifiability;
* narrow claims;
* explicit uncertainty;
* causal decomposition;
* source-grounded evidence;
* independently frozen procedures;
* adversarial protocol testing;
* negative findings where warranted.

Remember the strongest lesson from the previous research phase:

A CORRECT ARCHITECTURE AND CORRECT IMPLEMENTATION CAN STILL PRODUCE A MEANINGLESS EXPERIMENT IF THE ENVIRONMENT DOES NOT CONTAIN THE FAILURE MECHANISM BEING TESTED.

Before declaring the protocol ready, answer:

1. What exact failure mechanism is being tested?

2. Does the artifact population instantiate it?

3. Is the mechanism measurable?

4. Can adjacent failure mechanisms be distinguished?

5. What evidence would count against the current boundary hypothesis?

6. What bias might the diagnostic itself introduce?

7. Could the protocol produce a reassuring result while still failing to detect important semantic loss?

If the answer to question 7 is YES, the protocol is not ready until that failure mode is explicitly addressed.

Proceed with read-only protocol design and produce the required report.

Creating more metrics instead of resolving uncertainty.

DOCUMENTATION LOOPING

Producing artifacts without changing knowledge or capability.

SCOPE DRIFT

Moving toward interesting problems unrelated to EkamNet v0.1.

ARCHITECTURAL ACCRETION

Adding abstractions faster than evidence requires them.

STATE DRIFT

Allowing canonical state files to diverge from code and evidence.

POSITIVE

NEGATIVE

---

## SELECTION RISK POSITIVE

The environment demonstrates measurable Selection Optimism or Winner's Curse under the frozen procedure.

Selection Risk is causally instantiated strongly enough to evaluate safeguards.

Not permitted:

Prospective Validation works.

## SELECTION RISK NEGATIVE

The environment is capable of exposing Selection Risk, but the pre-registered meaningful effect is not observed.

Interpret narrowly.

Do not automatically conclude selection is safe.

---

## SELECTION RISK INCONCLUSIVE

The environment or evidence cannot distinguish absence of Selection Risk from insufficient mechanism strength or experimental sensitivity.

---

## PROSPECTIVE VALIDATION POSITIVE

Only after Selection Risk is demonstrated:

Prospective Validation measurably reduces the target failure mechanism under the frozen environment.

Permitted implication:

Prospective Validation demonstrates protection against the observed Selection Risk under the tested environment.

Not permitted:

Prospective Validation is universally validated.

---

## PROSPECTIVE VALIDATION NEGATIVE

Selection Risk is demonstrated, but Prospective Validation fails to provide the pre-registered protection.

Preserve the negative result.

Do not tune the safeguard after observing results.

---

## NO_DIFFERENCE

Use only when a genuine comparison exists, minimum meaningful effect is pre-registered, experimental sensitivity is adequate, and no meaningful difference is detected.

11. REQUIRED INVARIANTS
=======================

At minimum investigate:

IDENTITY INVARIANT

The same belief remains identifiable across longitudinal updates.

PROVENANCE INVARIANT

Every state change records why it occurred.

TEMPORAL INVARIANT

Later evidence cannot appear to precede earlier belief state.

IDEMPOTENCY INVARIANT

Applying the same evidence twice does not create duplicate epistemic change unless explicitly intended.

CAUSAL ATTRIBUTION INVARIANT

Without the triggering evidence, the state transition does not occur.

CONTRADICTION RESPONSIVENESS INVARIANT

Material contradicting evidence can weaken the belief.

SUPPORT RESPONSIVENESS INVARIANT

Material supporting evidence does not incorrectly weaken the belief.

HISTORY PRESERVATION INVARIANT

Prior epistemic state remains auditable after transition.

Do not add invariants unrelated to the current scientific question.

3. EPOCH 8 PRIMARY OBJECTIVE
============================

The primary objective is to instantiate and scientifically test the smallest causal chain:

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE EXISTS

→

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE PERSISTS

→

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE IS RELEVANT TO A FUTURE COGNITIVE EVENT

→

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE IS RETRIEVED

→

RETRIEVED EXPERIENCE ENTERS FUTURE COGNITION

→

FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR CHANGES

→

THE CHANGE IS CAUSALLY ATTRIBUTABLE TO THE PAST EXPERIENCE.

Then determine:

DID THE CHANGE IMPROVE, DEGRADE, OR LEAVE UNCHANGED FUTURE EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE?

The minimal target is:

ONE PAST EPISTEMIC OUTCOME

→

ONE FUTURE COGNITIVE DECISION

→

======================================================================
4. CRITICAL DEFINITION OF LEARNING
==================================

For Epoch 8:

LEARNING IS NOT:

DATA STORED.

LEARNING IS NOT:

MEMORY RETRIEVED.

LEARNING IS NOT:

A PROMPT CONTAINS PAST CONTEXT.

LEARNING IS NOT:

BEHAVIOR CHANGED FOR AN UNKNOWN REASON.

The minimum operational definition is:

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE CAUSALLY CHANGES FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR.

A stronger positive result is:

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE CAUSALLY CHANGES FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR AND IMPROVES FUTURE EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE.

A negative but scientifically important result is:

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE IS STORED AND RETRIEVED BUT DOES NOT CHANGE FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR.

Another negative result is:

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE CHANGES FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR BUT DEGRADES FUTURE EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE.

Preserve all outcomes.

======================================================================
5. PRIMARY EPOCH 8 FAILURE MECHANISMS
=====================================

Investigate the following failure mechanisms.

FAILURE A:

MEMORY_WITHOUT_RETRIEVAL.

Past experience persists but is not retrieved when relevant.

FAILURE B:

RETRIEVAL_WITHOUT_INFLUENCE.

Past experience is retrieved but future cognition behaves identically.

FAILURE C:

INFLUENCE_WITHOUT_ATTRIBUTION.

Future behavior changes, but the change cannot be causally attributed to past experience.

FAILURE D:

HARMFUL_LEARNING.

Past experience causally changes future cognition but reduces epistemic performance.

FAILURE E:

MEMORY_LEAKAGE_OR_CONDITION_CONTAMINATION.

Control conditions receive information from past experience.

FAILURE F:

RETRIEVAL_ORACLE_CONTAMINATION.

The retrieval mechanism uses information unavailable at the future decision point.

FAILURE G:

DEFERRED_EXPERIENCE_STRANDING.

A previously deferred true-causal candidate receives relevant later evidence but cannot influence future cognition because the past outcome is inaccessible or unusable.

Do not assume Failure G currently exists.

Test only if repository reality supports a clean experiment.

======================================================================

8. DEFERRED-CANDIDATE TEST FAMILY
=================================

The following question is explicitly open:

CAN A PREVIOUSLY DEFERRED TRUE_CAUSAL CANDIDATE EVENTUALLY INFLUENCE FUTURE COGNITION WHEN NEW CONFIRMING EVIDENCE ARRIVES?

Current state:

NOT_DEMONSTRATED_TO_WORK.

Possible causal chain:

T1:

CANDIDATE IS DEFERRED DUE TO INSUFFICIENT PROSPECTIVE EVIDENCE.

T2:

DEFERRED OUTCOME PERSISTS.

T3:

NEW RELEVANT CONFIRMING EVIDENCE BECOMES AVAILABLE.

T4:

PAST DEFERRED EXPERIENCE IS OR IS NOT RETRIEVED.

T5:

FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR IS OR IS NOT ALTERED.

T6:

FUTURE EPISTEMIC OUTCOME IS MEASURED.

9. REQUIRED CAUSAL LADDER
=========================

The experiment must separately evaluate:

LEVEL 1:

EXPERIENCE EXISTS.

LEVEL 2:

EXPERIENCE PERSISTS.

EXPERIENCE IS RETRIEVABLE.

LEVEL 4:

EXPERIENCE IS ACTUALLY RETRIEVED.

RETRIEVED EXPERIENCE IS AVAILABLE TO FUTURE COGNITION.

LEVEL 6:

FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR CHANGES.

LEVEL 7:

THE CHANGE IS CAUSALLY ATTRIBUTABLE TO THE EXPERIENCE.

LEVEL 8:

THE CHANGE IMPROVES, DEGRADES, OR LEAVES UNCHANGED EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE.

Do not collapse these levels into one metric.

Report the highest level actually demonstrated.

======================================================================
10. REQUIRED EXPERIMENTAL CONDITIONS
====================================

Prefer the following four-condition design if repository reality supports clean isolation.

CONDITION A — NO PAST EXPERIENCE CONTROL

The future cognitive event occurs without the relevant past epistemic experience existing.

Purpose:

establish baseline future behavior.

CONDITION B — EXPERIENCE EXISTS BUT IS NOT RETRIEVED

The relevant past epistemic experience exists and persists but is intentionally unavailable to retrieval.

Purpose:

separate storage from retrieval.

CONDITION C — EXPERIENCE RETRIEVED BUT INFLUENCE BLOCKED

The relevant past epistemic experience is retrieved and observable, but an experiment boundary prevents it from altering the selected future cognitive behavior.

Purpose:

separate retrieval from influence.

CONDITION D — EXPERIENCE RETRIEVED AND INFLUENCE ENABLED

The relevant past epistemic experience is retrieved and allowed to affect the selected future cognitive behavior.

Purpose:

test causal influence.

The primary causal comparison is:

CONDITION C

versus

CONDITION D.

These conditions should differ only in whether retrieved experience is allowed to influence future cognition.

Secondary comparisons:

A versus B:

does mere existence or storage create contamination?

B versus C:

does retrieval itself change behavior despite influence being blocked?

C versus D:

does cognitive influence causally change future behavior?

Then measure epistemic performance.

If the full four-condition design is not repository-native:

use the smallest alternative design that preserves the causal distinctions.

Document why.

24. DEFERRED-CANDIDATE CONSTRAINT
=================================

If the deferred-candidate family is used:

do not silently implement full re-entry.

The primary question should be framed as:

CAN PAST DEFERRED EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE BE RETRIEVED AND CAUSALLY INFLUENCE A FUTURE COGNITIVE DECISION WHEN NEW RELEVANT EVIDENCE ARRIVES?

This is not identical to:

CAN THE SAME DEFERRED CANDIDATE AUTOMATICALLY REENTER THE LIFECYCLE?

The first tests learning.

The second requires lifecycle architecture.

Keep them separate.

If retrieval of deferred experience changes future candidate generation, ranking, evidence acquisition, or reconsideration behavior:

that may demonstrate causal learning even without full candidate re-entry.

26. AUTONOMOUS CONTINUATION LOGIC
=================================

MINIMAL_CAUSAL_LEARNING_DEMONSTRATED_WITH_NEGATIVE_EPISTEMIC_EFFECT.

AUTONOMOUS RESEARCH-ENGINEERING EPOCH 8

Target:

MILESTONE 7 — MINIMAL CAUSAL LEARNING LOOP

The governing scientific question is:

CAN PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE CAUSALLY AND MEASURABLY CHANGE FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR?

The stronger secondary question is:

WHEN PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE CHANGES FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR, DOES THAT CHANGE IMPROVE, DEGRADE, OR LEAVE UNCHANGED FUTURE EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE?

Do not attempt to implement the complete final DP/EkamNet learning architecture.

Do not begin by building Lesson Formation, Principle Formation, Revival, Succession, or a generalized closed-loop cognitive framework.

Find and test the smallest repository-native causal learning loop first.

2. PROGRAM-LEVEL LESSONS THAT GOVERN EPOCH 8
============================================

Epoch 8 must internalize the following lessons.

LESSON 1:

TESTS PASSING DOES NOT IMPLY SCIENTIFIC VALIDITY.

LESSON 2:

METHODOLOGICAL EVIDENCE EXISTING DOES NOT IMPLY THE CLAIM IS SUPPORTED.

LESSON 3:

MEMORY STORAGE DOES NOT IMPLY RETRIEVAL.

LESSON 4:

RETRIEVAL DOES NOT IMPLY COGNITIVE INFLUENCE.

LESSON 5:

COGNITIVE INFLUENCE DOES NOT IMPLY BENEFICIAL LEARNING.

LESSON 6:

AN ABSENT CAPABILITY DOES NOT BY ITSELF DEMONSTRATE A CAUSAL FAILURE.

LESSON 7:

A PRE_REGISTERED PREDICTION MUST EXIST IN A PERSISTENT, AUDITABLE ARTIFACT BEFORE EXECUTION.

AG reasoning context alone does not count as scientific pre-registration.

======================================================================
3. EPOCH 8 PRIMARY OBJECTIVE
============================

The primary objective is to instantiate and scientifically test the smallest causal chain:

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE EXISTS

→

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE PERSISTS

→

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE IS RELEVANT TO A FUTURE COGNITIVE EVENT

→

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE IS RETRIEVED

→

RETRIEVED EXPERIENCE ENTERS FUTURE COGNITION

→

FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR CHANGES

→

THE CHANGE IS CAUSALLY ATTRIBUTABLE TO THE PAST EXPERIENCE.

Then determine:

DID THE CHANGE IMPROVE, DEGRADE, OR LEAVE UNCHANGED FUTURE EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE?

The minimal target is:

ONE PAST EPISTEMIC OUTCOME

→

ONE FUTURE COGNITIVE DECISION

→

ONE MEASURABLE CAUSAL EFFECT.

Do not build more than is necessary to test this.

======================================================================
4. CRITICAL DEFINITION OF LEARNING
==================================

For Epoch 8:

LEARNING IS NOT:

DATA STORED.

LEARNING IS NOT:

MEMORY RETRIEVED.

LEARNING IS NOT:

A PROMPT CONTAINS PAST CONTEXT.

LEARNING IS NOT:

BEHAVIOR CHANGED FOR AN UNKNOWN REASON.

The minimum operational definition is:

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE CAUSALLY CHANGES FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR.

A stronger positive result is:

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE CAUSALLY CHANGES FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR AND IMPROVES FUTURE EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE.

A negative but scientifically important result is:

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE IS STORED AND RETRIEVED BUT DOES NOT CHANGE FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR.

Another negative result is:

PAST EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE CHANGES FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR BUT DEGRADES FUTURE EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE.

Preserve all outcomes.

======================================================================
5. PRIMARY EPOCH 8 FAILURE MECHANISMS
=====================================

Investigate the following failure mechanisms.

FAILURE A:

MEMORY_WITHOUT_RETRIEVAL.

Past experience persists but is not retrieved when relevant.

FAILURE B:

RETRIEVAL_WITHOUT_INFLUENCE.

Past experience is retrieved but future cognition behaves identically.

FAILURE C:

INFLUENCE_WITHOUT_ATTRIBUTION.

Future behavior changes, but the change cannot be causally attributed to past experience.

FAILURE D:

HARMFUL_LEARNING.

Past experience causally changes future cognition but reduces epistemic performance.

FAILURE E:

MEMORY_LEAKAGE_OR_CONDITION_CONTAMINATION.

Control conditions receive information from past experience.

FAILURE F:

RETRIEVAL_ORACLE_CONTAMINATION.

The retrieval mechanism uses information unavailable at the future decision point.

FAILURE G:

DEFERRED_EXPERIENCE_STRANDING.

A previously deferred true-causal candidate receives relevant later evidence but cannot influence future cognition because the past outcome is inaccessible or unusable.

Do not assume Failure G currently exists.

Test only if repository reality supports a clean experiment.

14. whether prior selection outcomes are retrievable;

15. whether prior evidence outcomes are retrievable;

16. whether retrieved experience currently enters any future decision;

17. whether causal intervention can be isolated behind a feature flag or experiment boundary;

18. whether deterministic or frozen-world experiments can support the required comparison;

19. whether an existing cognitive decision provides the smallest measurable intervention point;

20. whether the current architecture already contains a partial causal learning loop that has never been scientifically tested.

Produce a repository reality map before implementing anything.

8. DEFERRED-CANDIDATE TEST FAMILY
=================================

The following question is explicitly open:

CAN A PREVIOUSLY DEFERRED TRUE_CAUSAL CANDIDATE EVENTUALLY INFLUENCE FUTURE COGNITION WHEN NEW CONFIRMING EVIDENCE ARRIVES?

Current state:

NOT_DEMONSTRATED_TO_WORK.

NOT_DEMONSTRATED_TO_FAIL.

If repository reality shows this is the smallest clean causal learning-loop experiment, it may be selected as the primary test family.

Possible causal chain:

T0:

TRUE_CAUSAL CANDIDATE EXISTS.

T1:

CANDIDATE IS DEFERRED DUE TO INSUFFICIENT PROSPECTIVE EVIDENCE.

T2:

DEFERRED OUTCOME PERSISTS.

T3:

NEW RELEVANT CONFIRMING EVIDENCE BECOMES AVAILABLE.

T4:

PAST DEFERRED EXPERIENCE IS OR IS NOT RETRIEVED.

T5:

FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR IS OR IS NOT ALTERED.

T6:

FUTURE EPISTEMIC OUTCOME IS MEASURED.

However:

do not force this test family if another repository-native intervention provides a cleaner first causal demonstration.

If deferred-candidate re-evaluation requires a major new lifecycle architecture:

do not implement it merely to satisfy this prompt.

Record the constraint and choose a smaller intervention.

9. REQUIRED CAUSAL LADDER
=========================

The experiment must separately evaluate:

LEVEL 1:

EXPERIENCE EXISTS.

LEVEL 2:

EXPERIENCE PERSISTS.

LEVEL 3:

EXPERIENCE IS RETRIEVABLE.

LEVEL 4:

EXPERIENCE IS ACTUALLY RETRIEVED.

LEVEL 5:

RETRIEVED EXPERIENCE IS AVAILABLE TO FUTURE COGNITION.

LEVEL 6:

FUTURE COGNITIVE BEHAVIOR CHANGES.

LEVEL 7:

THE CHANGE IS CAUSALLY ATTRIBUTABLE TO THE EXPERIENCE.

LEVEL 8:

THE CHANGE IMPROVES, DEGRADES, OR LEAVES UNCHANGED EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE.

Do not collapse these levels into one metric.

Report the highest level actually demonstrated.

======================================================================
10. REQUIRED EXPERIMENTAL CONDITIONS
====================================

Prefer the following four-condition design if repository reality supports clean isolation.

CONDITION A — NO PAST EXPERIENCE CONTROL

The future cognitive event occurs without the relevant past epistemic experience existing.

Purpose:

establish baseline future behavior.

CONDITION B — EXPERIENCE EXISTS BUT IS NOT RETRIEVED

The relevant past epistemic experience exists and persists but is intentionally unavailable to retrieval.

Purpose:

separate storage from retrieval.

CONDITION C — EXPERIENCE RETRIEVED BUT INFLUENCE BLOCKED

The relevant past epistemic experience is retrieved and observable, but an experiment boundary prevents it from altering the selected future cognitive behavior.

Purpose:

separate retrieval from influence.

CONDITION D — EXPERIENCE RETRIEVED AND INFLUENCE ENABLED

The relevant past epistemic experience is retrieved and allowed to affect the selected future cognitive behavior.

Purpose:

test causal influence.

The primary causal comparison is:

CONDITION C

versus

CONDITION D.

These conditions should differ only in whether retrieved experience is allowed to influence future cognition.

Secondary comparisons:

A versus B:

does mere existence or storage create contamination?

B versus C:

does retrieval itself change behavior despite influence being blocked?

C versus D:

does cognitive influence causally change future behavior?

Then measure epistemic performance.

If the full four-condition design is not repository-native:

use the smallest alternative design that preserves the causal distinctions.

Document why.

14. CAUSAL NECESSITY BEFORE SAFEGUARD OR CAPABILITY CLAIMS
==========================================================

Before evaluating whether memory improves future cognition, demonstrate that the experimental environment can instantiate a meaningful behavioral difference.

The environment must permit:

A FUTURE COGNITIVE DECISION

where:

PAST EXPERIENCE COULD REASONABLY CHANGE THE DECISION.

Avoid trivial experiments where:

the future answer is deterministic regardless of memory;

the memory merely repeats the correct answer;

the treatment directly injects an oracle label;

the treatment exposes future evidence;

the behavior metric cannot vary.

Establish causal necessity before scaling.

22. REQUIRED NEGATIVE CONTROLS
==============================

Include controls capable of exposing false learning claims.

At minimum consider:

IRRELEVANT_MEMORY_CONTROL

where unrelated past experience is retrieved.

Expected:

no justified improvement attributable to relevant learning.

SHAM_RETRIEVAL_CONTROL

where retrieval infrastructure executes but returns no relevant experience.

Expected:

behavior should match the appropriate no-influence baseline.

INFLUENCE_BLOCKED_CONTROL

where relevant memory is retrieved but prevented from entering future cognition.

Expected:

separates retrieval from influence.

Choose only controls needed for causal identification.

Do not inflate experiment size unnecessarily.

======================================================================
24. DEFERRED-CANDIDATE CONSTRAINT
=================================

If the deferred-candidate family is used:

do not silently implement full re-entry.

The primary question should be framed as:

CAN PAST DEFERRED EPISTEMIC EXPERIENCE BE RETRIEVED AND CAUSALLY INFLUENCE A FUTURE COGNITIVE DECISION WHEN NEW RELEVANT EVIDENCE ARRIVES?

This is not identical to:

CAN THE SAME DEFERRED CANDIDATE AUTOMATICALLY REENTER THE LIFECYCLE?

The first tests learning.

The second requires lifecycle architecture.

Keep them separate.

If retrieval of deferred experience changes future candidate generation, ranking, evidence acquisition, or reconsideration behavior:

that may demonstrate causal learning even without full candidate re-entry.

26. AUTONOMOUS CONTINUATION LOGIC
=================================

CASE A:

REPOSITORY ALREADY CONTAINS A PARTIAL LEARNING LOOP.

Then:

instrument it;

isolate it;

pre-register;

test it.

CASE B:

ONE SMALL MISSING ADAPTER PREVENTS THE LOOP.

Then:

implement the adapter reversibly;

test it;

execute the experiment.

CASE C:

DEFERRED EXPERIENCE IS THE CLEANEST TEST FAMILY.

Then:

use it while preserving the distinction between:

MEMORY_INFLUENCE

and

LIFECYCLE_REENTRY.

CASE D:

ANOTHER TEST FAMILY PROVIDES CLEANER CAUSAL IDENTIFICATION.

Then:

use the cleaner family.

Document why.

CASE E:

PAST EXPERIENCE IS RETRIEVED BUT DOES NOT CHANGE FUTURE COGNITION.

Then:

record:

MEMORY_RETRIEVAL_DEMONSTRATED_WITHOUT_CAUSAL_BEHAVIOR_CHANGE.

Do not force an implementation repair unless a specific defect is demonstrated.

CASE F:

PAST EXPERIENCE CHANGES FUTURE COGNITION BUT HARMS PERFORMANCE.

Then:

record:

MINIMAL_CAUSAL_LEARNING_DEMONSTRATED_WITH_NEGATIVE_EPISTEMIC_EFFECT.

Do not suppress the negative result.

CASE G:

PAST EXPERIENCE CHANGES FUTURE COGNITION AND IMPROVES PERFORMANCE.

Then:

record:

MINIMAL_CAUSAL_LEARNING_DEMONSTRATED_WITH_POSITIVE_EPISTEMIC_EFFECT.

Do not claim:

GENERALIZED LEARNING.

LESSON FORMATION.

PRINCIPLE FORMATION.

SELF_IMPROVEMENT.

================================

Before finalizing the Epoch report:

verify:

1. all predictions claimed as pre-registered exist in a persistent artifact created before primary execution;

2. no diagnostic result is represented as primary evidence;

3. no memory persistence claim is represented as retrieval;

6. no behavioral difference is called causal without condition isolation;

7. no deferred-candidate result is represented as lifecycle re-entry unless actual re-entry occurred;

8. no structural possibility is represented as causal demonstration;

9. every critical claim passes ClaimEvidenceConsistencyGate;

10. no stale verdict string is copied from prior Epochs;

11. canonical state matches the report;

12. capability map matches demonstrated evidence maturity;

13. test counts are consistent;

14. no critical FAIL or INDETERMINATE gate is hidden by the final verdict.

# AG AUTONOMOUS RESEARCH-ENGINEERING LOOP FRAMEWORK v1.0
## DP/EkamNet Program — Standing Operating Contract

This framework governs how you operate within an epoch. It stays in effect
across epochs unless explicitly amended. Read it in full before starting
any epoch that references it.

======================================================================
1. AUTONOMY ZONE — no permission needed
======================================================================

Within an authorized epoch objective, you may without stopping:

- Inspect repository state, run diagnostics, read artifacts.
- Write, run, and iterate on code within the ALREADY-AUTHORIZED scope
  (i.e. scope explicitly named in the current epoch's objective section).
- Fix bugs you discover, including in your own prior-iteration code.
- Add or adjust unit tests.
- Run diagnostic/pilot-scale experiments explicitly permitted by the
  current epoch's design.
- Self-correct: if you find a flaw in your own reasoning, comparator,
  isolation, or measurement mid-epoch, fix it and continue. Log it as a
  discovered-and-corrected defect, not a stopping event.
- Iterate up to the epoch's stated maximum iterations.

======================================================================
2. HARD STOPS — always require human review before proceeding
======================================================================

You MUST stop and produce a report, without proceeding further, when
any of the following occurs:

STOP-1: IMPLEMENTING OUTSIDE A FROZEN DESIGN
  You are about to build a capability (e.g. a selection engine, a new
  primitive, a new comparator, a new experiment mechanism) that was not
  explicitly named and scoped in a previously frozen paper design or the
  current epoch's authorized objective. Building it "because it's the
  obvious next step" is not authorization.

STOP-2: MILESTONE OR EPOCH CLOSURE
  You are about to write a closure report, mark a milestone complete, or
  update canonical program state with a completion status. This always
  requires human review before the status is written as final, even if
  all internal gates report PASS.

STOP-3: CLAIM LANGUAGE
  Your report is about to use words including but not limited to:
  "demonstrated," "validated," "proven," "complete," "protection,"
  "confirmed," "established," "verified" (in the scientific-claim sense,
  not the code-fact sense) applied to any capability, safeguard, or
  hypothesis. Draft the finding, flag the claim language, and stop before
  finalizing.

STOP-4: VERDICT / LABEL INTO CANONICAL STATE
  Any string that will be written into EKAMNET_PROGRAM_STATE.md,
  EKAMNET_DECISION_JOURNAL.md, EKAMNET_CAPABILITY_MAP.md, or an epoch
  report's executive verdict field requires review before being
  committed as canonical, even if it was auto-generated by a completion
  gate.

STOP-5: SCOPE OR PARAMETER AMBIGUITY
  A specification, prior epoch report, or canonical artifact is
  ambiguous, missing, or internally contradictory, and proceeding would
  require you to invent an interpretation. Report the ambiguity; do not
  resolve it unilaterally.

STOP-6: NEGATIVE OR INCONCLUSIVE RESULT AT A DECISION POINT
  An experiment or gate produces a result that would change the
  program's roadmap direction (e.g. a safeguard shows no benefit, a
  mechanism fails to instantiate, a hypothesis is falsified). Report it
  plainly. Do not soften it, reframe it, or silently substitute a
  narrower successful sub-claim in its place.

======================================================================
3. MANDATORY SELF-CHECKS BEFORE ANY STOP-2/3/4 REPORT
======================================================================

Before producing a closure report or claim, verify and explicitly state:

A. VERDICT INTEGRITY CHECK
   Every verdict/label string in this report was generated fresh for
   THIS report. None were copied from a prior epoch, milestone, or
   audit. State this explicitly, do not just imply it.

B. CLAIM-EVIDENCE MATCH CHECK
   For every claim using STOP-3 language, quote the exact underlying
   numbers/comparison it rests on, and confirm the numbers actually
   support the strength of language used. If a metric moved but doesn't
   support the stated claim (e.g. "resource saved" being reported as
   "causal learning demonstrated"), downgrade the language before
   presenting it, and flag that a downgrade occurred.

C. MECHANISM CHECK
   State in one sentence what was ACTUALLY measured or built, in plain
   terms, separate from what the milestone SET OUT to measure or build.
   If these two sentences describe different things, this is a STOP-1
   or STOP-3 situation — say so explicitly rather than let the report's
   title imply they're the same.

D. SAMPLE SIZE / EVIDENCE SUFFICIENCY CHECK
   State the n involved in any quantitative claim. If n is small enough
   that the finding could plausibly be wiring-verification rather than
   a scientific result, say so explicitly and do not use STOP-3 language
   for it.

E. RUN THE ClaimEvidenceConsistencyGate (or current equivalent)
   explicitly against this report's own claims before presenting them,
   and report its PASS/FAIL output alongside the claim, not just
   internally.

======================================================================
4. REPORT FORMAT AT ANY STOP
======================================================================

When you hit a hard stop, produce a short report (not a full epoch
report) containing:

- STOP TYPE (1-6)
- WHAT TRIGGERED IT
- WHAT WAS ACTUALLY BUILT/MEASURED (plain sentence, per 3.C)
- WHAT WAS CLAIMED OR ABOUT TO BE CLAIMED
- SELF-CHECK RESULTS (A-E above, as applicable)
- OPTIONS: 2-4 concrete paths forward, with tradeoffs
- YOUR RECOMMENDATION (clearly marked as a recommendation, not a
  decision)

Then stop. Do not proceed, do not implement your recommendation, do not
mark anything complete. Wait for explicit human direction.

======================================================================
5. WHAT THIS FRAMEWORK DOES NOT CHANGE
======================================================================

- Epoch objectives, scope, and iteration bounds are still set per-epoch
  by the epoch-specific prompt.
- Frozen paper designs, methodology invariants, and canonical state
  remain authoritative and are not to be silently reinterpreted.
- "Do not roll back working code" still applies — hard stops pause
  forward progress and claims, not preservation of already-built,
  already-tested capability.

======================================================================
6. RATIONALE (for your own calibration, not to be repeated in reports)
======================================================================

Prior epochs in this program have shown a consistent pattern: mid-epoch
self-correction is reliable, but end-of-epoch claims have repeatedly
been stronger than the evidence supported (verdict-string
contamination across two audits, an implementation built without an
authorizing design, a 0%-vs-0% result reported as a demonstrated safety
benefit, a single-sequence experiment reported as order-sensitivity
verification, and compilation-time trigger caching reported as causal
learning). This framework is designed to keep the parts of the loop
that have worked (autonomous iteration, self-correction, bug-fixing)
while re-inserting review at exactly the points that have repeatedly
needed it (closure, claims, canonical state, scope authorization).
Nothing here is about distrust of the engineering work — the code has
consistently been solid. It's specifically about the gap between what
gets built and what gets claimed about what was built.
</USER_REQUEST>

X BECOMES TRUE_CAUSAL OR EPISTEMICALLY NECESSARY.

CONDITION D RETRIEVES MEMORY AND ENABLES PRUNING.

T7:

COMPARE PRIMARY EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE.

If Condition D performs worse because X was pruned:

classify:

NEGATIVE_MEMORY_OVERGENERALIZATION_CAUSALLY_DEMONSTRATED.

If no degradation occurs:

do not claim the risk is resolved unless the tested evidence is sufficient under the frozen protocol.

6. PRIMARY FAILURE MECHANISM
============================

The primary failure mechanism is:

NEGATIVE_MEMORY_OVERGENERALIZATION.

Operational form:

TRIGGER X IS NON_CAUSAL IN PAST CONTEXT A

→

PROPOSITION USING X IS REJECTED_OR_RETIRED

→

X IS STORED AS NEGATIVE EPISTEMIC MEMORY

→

FUTURE CONTEXT B ARRIVES

→

X IS NOW GENUINELY CAUSAL OR USEFUL

→

GLOBAL MEMORY-DRIVEN PRUNING REMOVES X BEFORE EVALUATION

→

TRUE CAUSAL CANDIDATE IS LOST

→

FUTURE EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE DEGRADES.

The competing beneficial mechanism is:

USEFUL_NEGATIVE_MEMORY.

Operational form:

TRIGGER X IS NON_CAUSAL IN PAST CONTEXT A

→

PROPOSITION USING X IS REJECTED_OR_RETIRED

→

X IS STORED AS NEGATIVE EPISTEMIC MEMORY

→

FUTURE CONTEXT B ARRIVES

→

X REMAINS NON_CAUSAL

→

MEMORY-DRIVEN PRUNING REMOVES X

→

FALSE OR USELESS CANDIDATE PROCESSING IS AVOIDED

→

RESOURCE USE MAY DECREASE

→

FUTURE EPISTEMIC PERFORMANCE IS PRESERVED OR IMPROVED.

The experiment must discriminate between these mechanisms.
